### Biodiversity

Main articles: [Forestry in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forestry_in_India "Forestry in India") and [Wildlife of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wildlife_of_India "Wildlife of India")

India is a [megadiverse country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megadiverse_country "Megadiverse country"), a term employed for 17 countries that host high [biological diversity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_diversity "Biological diversity") and contain many species [indigenous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indigenous_(ecology) "Indigenous (ecology)"), or [endemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endemic "Endemic"), to them.[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-207) India is the [habitat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habitat "Habitat") for 8.6% of all [mammals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mammal "Mammal"), 13.7% of [bird](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bird "Bird") species, 7.9% of [reptile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reptile "Reptile") species, 6% of [amphibian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amphibian "Amphibian") species, 12.2% of [fish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fish "Fish") species, and 6.0% of all [flowering plant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flowering_plant "Flowering plant") species.[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-208)[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Puri-209) Fully a third of Indian plant species are endemic.[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBasak198324-210) India also overlaps four of the world's 34 [biodiversity hotspots](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biodiversity_hotspot "Biodiversity hotspot"),[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-IUCN-India-211) or regions that display significant habitat loss in the presence of high endemism.[[t]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-213)[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-SivaperumanVenkataraman2018-212)

India's most dense forests, such as the [tropical moist forest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_and_subtropical_moist_broadleaf_forest "Tropical and subtropical moist broadleaf forest") of the [Andaman Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andaman_Islands "Andaman Islands"), the [Western Ghats](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Ghats "Western Ghats"), and [Northeast India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northeast_India "Northeast India"), occupy approximately 3% of its land area.[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Jha2018-214)[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-indiaforest-215) *Moderately dense forest*, whose canopy density is between 40% and 70%, occupies 9.39% of India's land area.[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Jha2018-214)[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-indiaforest-215) It predominates in the [temperate coniferous forest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperate_coniferous_forest "Temperate coniferous forest") of the [Himalayas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Himalaya "Himalaya"), the moist deciduous *[sal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shorea_robusta "Shorea robusta")* forest of eastern India, and the dry deciduous [teak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teak "Teak") forest of central and southern India.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTETritsch200111–12-216) India has two natural zones of [thorn forest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deserts_and_xeric_shrublands "Deserts and xeric shrublands"), one in the [Deccan Plateau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deccan_Plateau "Deccan Plateau"), immediately east of the Western Ghats, and the other in the western part of the Indo-Gangetic plain, now turned into rich agricultural land by irrigation, its features no longer visible.[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-217) Among the Indian subcontinent's notable indigenous trees are the [astringent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astringent "Astringent") *[Azadirachta indica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azadirachta_indica "Azadirachta indica")*, or *neem*, which is widely used in rural Indian [herbal medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herbal_medicine "Herbal medicine"),[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Goyal2006-218) and the luxuriant *[Ficus religiosa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ficus_religiosa "Ficus religiosa")*, or *peepul*,[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Hughes2013-219) which is displayed on the ancient seals of [Mohenjo-daro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohenjo-daro "Mohenjo-daro"),[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-AmeriCostello2018-220) and under which [the Buddha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gautama_Buddha "Gautama Buddha") is recorded in the [Pali canon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pāli_Canon "Pāli Canon") to have sought enlightenment.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Gwynne2011-221)

Many Indian species have descended from those of [Gondwana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gondwana "Gondwana"), the southern [supercontinent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supercontinent "Supercontinent") from which India separated more than 100 million years ago.[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrameOwen2002142-222) India's subsequent collision with Eurasia set off a mass exchange of species. However, [volcanism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deccan_Traps "Deccan Traps") and [climatic changes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_variability_and_change "Climate variability and change") later caused the extinction of many endemic Indian forms.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKaranth2006-223) Still later, mammals entered India from Asia through two [zoogeographic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoogeography "Zoogeography") passes flanking the Himalayas.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTETritsch200114-224) This lowered endemism among India's mammals, which stands at 12.6%, contrasting with 45.8% among reptiles and 55.8% among amphibians.[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Puri-209) Among endemics are the vulnerable[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-225) [hooded leaf monkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nilgiri_Langur "Nilgiri Langur")[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-itis-226) and the threatened [Beddome's toad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duttaphrynus_beddomii "Duttaphrynus beddomii")[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-IUCN-227)[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-228) of the Western Ghats.

India contains 172 [IUCN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Conservation_Union "World Conservation Union")-designated [threatened animal species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_endangered_animals_in_India "List of endangered animals in India"), or 2.9% of endangered forms.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIUCN1994xli-229) These include the endangered [Bengal tiger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bengal_tiger "Bengal tiger") and the [Ganges river dolphin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Asian_river_dolphin "South Asian river dolphin"). [Critically endangered](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Critically_endangered "Critically endangered") species include the [gharial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gharial "Gharial"), a [crocodilian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodilian "Crocodilian"); the [great Indian bustard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Indian_bustard "Great Indian bustard"); and the [Indian white-rumped vulture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White-rumped_vulture "White-rumped vulture"), which has become nearly extinct by having ingested the carrion of [diclofenac](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diclofenac "Diclofenac")-treated cattle.[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-LovetteFitzpatrick2016-230) Before they were extensively used for agriculture and cleared for human settlement, the thorn forests of Punjab were mingled at intervals with open grasslands that were grazed by large herds of [blackbuck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blackbuck_Conservation_Area "Blackbuck Conservation Area") preyed on by the [Asiatic cheetah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asiatic_cheetah "Asiatic cheetah"); the blackbuck, no longer extant in Punjab, is now severely endangered in India, and the cheetah is extinct.[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-231) The pervasive and ecologically devastating human encroachment of recent decades has critically endangered Indian wildlife. In response, the system of [national parks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_parks_of_India "National parks of India") and [protected areas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protected_areas_of_India "Protected areas of India"), first established in 1935, was expanded substantially. In 1972, India enacted the [Wildlife Protection Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wildlife_Protection_Act_of_1972 "Wildlife Protection Act of 1972")[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinistry_of_Environment_and_Forests_1972-232) and [Project Tiger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Project_Tiger "Project Tiger") to safeguard crucial wilderness; the Forest Conservation Act was enacted in 1980 and amendments added in 1988.[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDepartment_of_Environment_and_Forests1988-233) India hosts [more than five hundred wildlife sanctuaries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wildlife_sanctuaries_of_India "Wildlife sanctuaries of India") and [eighteen biosphere reserves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biosphere_reserves_of_India "Biosphere reserves of India"),[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-234) four of which are part of the [World Network of Biosphere Reserves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Network_of_Biosphere_Reserves "World Network of Biosphere Reserves"); its [eighty-nine wetlands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Ramsar_sites_in_India "List of Ramsar sites in India") are registered under the [Ramsar Convention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramsar_Convention "Ramsar Convention").[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-235)

- [![An Attacus taprobanis moth from Kadavoor, Kerala](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Attacus_taprobanis-Kadavoor-2018-07-07-001.jpg/330px-Attacus_taprobanis-Kadavoor-2018-07-07-001.jpg)](File:Attacus_taprobanis-Kadavoor-2018-07-07-001.jpg "An Attacus taprobanis moth from Kadavoor, Kerala")

  An *[Attacus taprobanis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attacus_taprobanis "Attacus taprobanis")* moth from [Kadavoor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kadavoor "Kadavoor"), [Kerala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerala "Kerala")
- [![India has the majority of the world's wild tigers, approximately 3,170 in 2022.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Bengal_tiger_in_Sanjay_Dubri_Tiger_Reserve_December_2024_by_Tisha_Mukherjee_11.jpg/330px-Bengal_tiger_in_Sanjay_Dubri_Tiger_Reserve_December_2024_by_Tisha_Mukherjee_11.jpg)](File:Bengal_tiger_in_Sanjay_Dubri_Tiger_Reserve_December_2024_by_Tisha_Mukherjee_11.jpg "India has the majority of the world's wild tigers, approximately 3,170 in 2022.")

  India has the majority of the world's wild [tigers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tiger "Tiger"), approximately 3,170 in 2022.[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-236)
- [![A purple sunbird perched on an Indian coral tree, Jim Corbett National Park, Uttarakhand](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/003_Purple_sunbird_in_Jim_Corbett_National_Park_Photo_by_Giles_Laurent.jpg/330px-003_Purple_sunbird_in_Jim_Corbett_National_Park_Photo_by_Giles_Laurent.jpg)](File:003_Purple_sunbird_in_Jim_Corbett_National_Park_Photo_by_Giles_Laurent.jpg "A purple sunbird perched on an Indian coral tree, Jim Corbett National Park, Uttarakhand")

  A [purple sunbird](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Purple_sunbird "Purple sunbird") perched on an [Indian coral tree](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_coral_tree "Indian coral tree"), [Jim Corbett National Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Corbett_National_Park "Jim Corbett National Park"), [Uttarakhand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uttarakhand "Uttarakhand")
- [![A Crested hawk-eagle with an Indian garden lizard in Satpura National Park, Madhya Pradesh](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Crested_hawk-eagle_%28Nisaetus_cirrhatus_cirrhatus%29_with_Indian_garden_lizard.jpg/250px-Crested_hawk-eagle_%28Nisaetus_cirrhatus_cirrhatus%29_with_Indian_garden_lizard.jpg)](File:Crested_hawk-eagle_(Nisaetus_cirrhatus_cirrhatus)_with_Indian_garden_lizard.jpg "A Crested hawk-eagle with an Indian garden lizard in Satpura National Park, Madhya Pradesh")

  A [Crested hawk-eagle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crested_hawk-eagle "Crested hawk-eagle") with an Indian [garden lizard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Garden_lizard "Garden lizard") in [Satpura National Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satpura_National_Park "Satpura National Park"), Madhya Pradesh
- [![Saltwater crocodile in Sundarbans National Park, West Bengal](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Saltwater_crocodile_in_Sundarbans_National_Park_November_2024_by_Tisha_Mukherjee_03.jpg/500px-Saltwater_crocodile_in_Sundarbans_National_Park_November_2024_by_Tisha_Mukherjee_03.jpg)](File:Saltwater_crocodile_in_Sundarbans_National_Park_November_2024_by_Tisha_Mukherjee_03.jpg "Saltwater crocodile in Sundarbans National Park, West Bengal")

  [Saltwater crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saltwater_crocodile "Saltwater crocodile") in [Sundarbans National Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sundarbans_National_Park "Sundarbans National Park"), [West Bengal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Bengal "West Bengal")

## Government and politics

### Politics

Main article: [Politics of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politics_of_India "Politics of India")

See also: [Democracy in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy_in_India "Democracy in India")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/The_Prime_Minister%2C_Shri_Narendra_Modi_addressing_the_inaugural_function_of_the_WCIT_India_2018_at_Hyderabad_via_video_conferencing_from_Misuru%2C_on_February_19%2C_2018_%281%29.jpg/250px-thumbnail.jpg)](File:The_Prime_Minister,_Shri_Narendra_Modi_addressing_the_inaugural_function_of_the_WCIT_India_2018_at_Hyderabad_via_video_conferencing_from_Misuru,_on_February_19,_2018_(1).jpg)

[Narendra Modi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narendra_Modi "Narendra Modi") has been India's Prime Minister since 2014.

India is a [parliamentary republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_republic "Parliamentary republic") with a [multi-party system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multi-party_system "Multi-party system").[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurnellCalvert1999125-237) There are six recognised [national parties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_India#National_parties "List of political parties in India") in the country, including the [Indian National Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_National_Congress "Indian National Congress") (generally, "the Congress") and the [Bharatiya Janata Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party "Bharatiya Janata Party") (BJP); there are over 50 [regional parties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_India#State_parties "List of political parties in India").[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEElection_Commission_of_India-238) The Congress is considered the [ideological centre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centrism "Centrism") in Indian [political culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_culture "Political culture");[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-239) the BJP is [right-wing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right-wing_politics "Right-wing politics") to [far-right](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far-right_politics "Far-right politics").

After India's independence on August 15, 1947, [Jawaharlal Nehru](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru "Jawaharlal Nehru") became prime minister of the [Dominion of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dominion_of_India "Dominion of India"), an office he held until January 26, 1950, when India became a republic; Nehru remained the caretaker prime minister until the following year.[[u]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-243) In the general elections in [1951](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1951_Indian_general_election "1951 Indian general election"), [1957](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1957_Indian_general_election "1957 Indian general election"), and [1962](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1962_Indian_general_election "1962 Indian general election"), the Congress, led by Nehru, won by comfortable margins. After Nehru [died](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_and_state_funeral_of_Jawaharlal_Nehru "Death and state funeral of Jawaharlal Nehru") in office in May 1964, [Lal Bahadur Shastri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lal_Bahadur_Shastri "Lal Bahadur Shastri") was unanimously chosen by the Congress to be parliamentary leader, and thus prime minister. After the [India–Pakistan war of 1965](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India–Pakistan_war_of_1965 "India–Pakistan war of 1965"), Shastri [died](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death_and_state_funeral_of_Lal_Bahadur_Shastri "Death and state funeral of Lal Bahadur Shastri") in January 1966, soon after signing the [Tashkent Peace Declaration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tashkent_Declaration "Tashkent Declaration"). The Congress chose [Indira Gandhi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indira_Gandhi "Indira Gandhi") to be prime minister. She led the party to election victories in [1967](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1967_Indian_general_election "1967 Indian general election") and [1971](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1971_Indian_general_election "1971 Indian general election"), the latter a [landslide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Landslide_victory "Landslide victory") after Pakistan's defeat in the [Bangladesh Liberation War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bangladesh_Liberation_War "Bangladesh Liberation War"). In 1975, Indira Gandhi declared a [state of emergency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Emergency_(India) "The Emergency (India)"), suspending many civil liberties. Following public discontent with the Emergency, the Congress was voted out of power in [1977](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1977_Indian_general_election "1977 Indian general election"); [Janata Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Janata_Party "Janata Party"), which had opposed the Emergency, was voted in. Its government lasted two years; [Morarji Desai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morarji_Desai "Morarji Desai") and [Charan Singh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charan_Singh "Charan Singh") served as prime ministers. The Congress returned to power in 1980. After a [military operation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Operation_Blue_Star "Operation Blue Star") against [Sikh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sikhs "Sikhs") militants occupying the [Golden Temple](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Temple "Golden Temple") in [Amritsar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amritsar "Amritsar"), Indira Gandhi was [assassinated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Indira_Gandhi "Assassination of Indira Gandhi") by a Sikh bodyguard on October 31, 1984. She was succeeded as prime minister by [Rajiv Gandhi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rajiv_Gandhi "Rajiv Gandhi"), who led Congress to a comfortable victory in the [elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1984_Indian_general_election "1984 Indian general election") at the end of the year. In 1989, a [National Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Front_(India) "National Front (India)") coalition, led by the [Janata Dal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Janata_Dal "Janata Dal"), in alliance with the [Left Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_India_(Marxist) "Communist Party of India (Marxist)"), won the [general elections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1989_Indian_general_election "1989 Indian general election"). The subsequent government lasted just under two years; [V. P. Singh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/V._P._Singh "V. P. Singh") and [Chandra Shekhar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chandra_Shekhar "Chandra Shekhar") served as prime ministers.[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBhambhri1992118,_143-244) In 1991, soon after the first round of polling in the [general election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Indian_general_election "1991 Indian general election"), Congress leader Rajiv Gandhi [was assassinated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Rajiv_Gandhi "Assassination of Rajiv Gandhi") by a member of a [Sri Lankan Tamil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sri_Lankan_Tamils "Sri Lankan Tamils") [separatist organisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberation_Tigers_of_Tamil_Eelam "Liberation Tigers of Tamil Eelam") who was seeking to avenge [Indian intervention in the Sri Lankan civil war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_intervention_in_the_Sri_Lankan_civil_war "Indian intervention in the Sri Lankan civil war"). After the elections, Congress emerged as the largest single party; a new Congress leader, [P. V. Narasimha Rao](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/P._V._Narasimha_Rao "P. V. Narasimha Rao"), formed a [minority government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minority_government "Minority government") which served a full five-year term.[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-245)

In 1996, the BJP briefly formed a government after winning the [general election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1996_Indian_general_election "1996 Indian general election"). [United Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Front_(India,_1996) "United Front (India, 1996)") coalition governments followed, which relied on external political support, [H. D. Deve Gowda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H._D._Deve_Gowda "H. D. Deve Gowda") and [I. K. Gujral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I._K._Gujral "I. K. Gujral") serving as prime ministers. After the [1998 Indian general election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998_Indian_general_election "1998 Indian general election"), [Atal Bihari Vajpayee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atal_Bihari_Vajpayee "Atal Bihari Vajpayee") of the BJP became prime minister; his government was short-lived due to the lack of a continued mandate. Elections were held again in [1999](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999_Indian_general_election "1999 Indian general election"). The BJP, now a part of the [National Democratic Alliance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Democratic_Alliance "National Democratic Alliance") (NDA), formed a coalition government led by Vajpayee, who became the first non-Congress prime minister to complete a five-year term.[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDunleavyDiwakarDunleavy2007-246) In the [2004 general election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_Indian_general_election "2004 Indian general election"), the NDA was defeated. Congress emerged as the largest single party and formed a coalition, the [United Progressive Alliance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Progressive_Alliance "United Progressive Alliance") (UPA). [Manmohan Singh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manmohan_Singh "Manmohan Singh"), a Sikh, who was proposed by Congress President [Sonia Gandhi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sonia_Gandhi "Sonia Gandhi") to be parliamentary leader, served as prime minister of the UPA government, but with some external support.[[v]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-247) The UPA returned to power in the [2009 general election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_Indian_general_election "2009 Indian general election") with increased numbers, no longer dependent on external support.[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKulkeRothermund2004384-248) Singh became the first prime minister to be re-elected after Jawaharlal Nehru in 1962.[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBusiness_Standard2009-249) In the [2014 general election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Indian_general_election "2014 Indian general election"), the BJP under [Narendra Modi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Narendra_Modi "Narendra Modi") became the first political party since 1984 to win an absolute majority.[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-250) The party won a larger majority in the [2019 general election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2019_Indian_general_election "2019 Indian general election"). After losing its majority in the [2024 general election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Indian_general_election "2024 Indian general election"), the BJP formed a coalition government with its NDA partners. Modi is the longest-serving non-Congress prime minister.[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-251) [Democratic backsliding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_backsliding "Democratic backsliding") was found by the 2026 [V-Dem Democracy Report](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/V-Dem_Institute#Democracy_Report "V-Dem Institute").[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-j496-252)

### Government

Main articles: [Government of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_India "Government of India"), [State governments of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_governments_of_India "State governments of India"), and [Local government in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Local_government_in_India "Local government in India")

See also: [Constitution of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_India "Constitution of India")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Constitution_of_India.jpg/250px-Constitution_of_India.jpg)](File:Constitution_of_India.jpg)

The original preamble of the [Constitution of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_India "Constitution of India") in 1950. In 1976, during the tenure of Indian prime minister [Indira Gandhi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indira_Gandhi "Indira Gandhi"), the first sentence was changed to "Sovereign Socialist Secular Democratic Republic".


The Constitution of India was drafted by the [Constituent Assembly of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constituent_Assembly_of_India "Constituent Assembly of India") with uncommon speed and absence of irregularities between 1946 and 1949.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpear1990242-253) The [Government of India Act 1935](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_India_Act_1935 "Government of India Act 1935") was used as a model and framework.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpear1990242-253) Long passages from the Act were included. The constitution describes a federal state with a parliamentary system of democracy.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpear1990242-253) The federal structure was conspicuous for the strength of the central government, which exclusively exercised control of defence, foreign affairs, railways, ports, and currency.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpear1990242-253) The President, the constitutional head of state, has reserve powers for taking over the administration of a state.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpear1990242-253) The central legislature has two houses: the *[Lok Sabha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lok_Sabha "Lok Sabha")*, whose delegates are directly elected by the people in general elections every five years, and the *[Rajya Sabha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rajya_Sabha "Rajya Sabha")*, whose members are nominated by the elected representatives in the states.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpear1990242-253) There are also features not to be found in the Act of 1935. The definition of fundamental rights is based on the [Constitution of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_United_States "Constitution of the United States"), and the constitutional directives, or goals of endeavor, are based on the [Constitution of Ireland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland "Constitution of Ireland").[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpear1990243-254) An Indian institution recommended by the constitution is the *[panchayat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panchayati_raj_in_India "Panchayati raj in India")* or village committees.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpear1990243-254) [Untouchability](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Untouchability "Untouchability") is illegal (Article 17) and caste distinctions are derecognized (Articles 15(2) and 16(2)).[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpear1990243-254) The promulgation of the Indian constitution transformed India into a republic within the Commonwealth.[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpear1990243-254)

The [prime minister of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_India "Prime Minister of India") is the [head of government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_government "Head of government") and exercises most [executive power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_(government) "Executive (government)").[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESharma1950-255) Appointed by the president,[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESharma2007162-256) the prime minister is supported by the [party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_party "Political party") or [political alliance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_alliance "Political alliance") with a majority of seats in the lower house of parliament.[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESharma1950-255) The executive of the Indian government consists of the president, the [vice-president](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vice_President_of_India "Vice President of India"), and the [Union Council of Ministers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_Council_of_Ministers "Union Council of Ministers")—with the [cabinet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_(government) "Cabinet (government)") being its executive committee—headed by the prime minister. Any minister holding a portfolio must be a member of one of the houses of parliament.[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESharma200731-257) In the Indian parliamentary system, the executive is subordinate to the legislature; the prime minister and their council are directly responsible to the lower house of the parliament. [Civil servants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_Services_of_India "Civil Services of India") act as permanent executives and all decisions of the executive are implemented by them.[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMathew2003524-258)

India has a three-tier unitary [independent judiciary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judicial_independence "Judicial independence")[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeuborne2003478-259) comprising the [supreme court](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_India "Supreme Court of India"), headed by the [Chief Justice of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_India "Chief Justice of India"), 25 [high courts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High_courts_of_India "High courts of India"), and a large number of trial courts.[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTENeuborne2003478-259) The supreme court has [original jurisdiction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Original_jurisdiction "Original jurisdiction") over cases involving [fundamental rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fundamental_rights_in_India "Fundamental rights in India") and over disputes between states and the centre and has [appellate jurisdiction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Appellate_jurisdiction "Appellate jurisdiction") over the high courts.[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESharma2007238,_255-260) It has the power to both strike down union or state laws which contravene the constitution[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESripati1998423–424-261) and invalidate any government action it deems unconstitutional.[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPylee2003b314-262)

### Administrative divisions

Main article: [Administrative divisions of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_India "Administrative divisions of India")

See also: [Political integration of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_integration_of_India "Political integration of India")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Political_map_of_India_EN.svg/250px-Political_map_of_India_EN.svg.png)

A clickable map of the 28 states and 8 union territories of India


India is a federal union comprising 28 [states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/States_and_union_territories_of_India "States and union territories of India") and 8 [union territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_territory "Union territory").[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress2004-19) All states, as well as the union territories of [Jammu and Kashmir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(union_territory) "Jammu and Kashmir (union territory)"), [Puducherry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puducherry_(union_territory) "Puducherry (union territory)") and the [National Capital Territory of Delhi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delhi "Delhi"), have elected legislatures and governments following the [Westminster system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Westminster_system "Westminster system"). The remaining five union territories are directly ruled by the central government through appointed administrators. In 1956, under the [States Reorganisation Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/States_Reorganisation_Act,_1956 "States Reorganisation Act, 1956"), states were reorganised on a linguistic basis.[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESharma200749-263) There are over a quarter of a million local government bodies at city, town, district, block and village levels.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-264)

#### States

- [Andhra Pradesh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh "Andhra Pradesh")
- [Arunachal Pradesh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arunachal_Pradesh "Arunachal Pradesh")
- [Assam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assam "Assam")
- [Bihar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bihar "Bihar")
- [Chhattisgarh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chhattisgarh "Chhattisgarh")
- [Goa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Goa "Goa")
- [Gujarat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gujarat "Gujarat")
- [Haryana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haryana "Haryana")
- [Himachal Pradesh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Himachal_Pradesh "Himachal Pradesh")
- [Jharkhand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jharkhand "Jharkhand")
- [Karnataka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karnataka "Karnataka")
- [Kerala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerala "Kerala")
- [Madhya Pradesh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madhya_Pradesh "Madhya Pradesh")
- [Maharashtra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maharashtra "Maharashtra")
- [Manipur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manipur "Manipur")

### Foreign relations

Main article: [Foreign relations of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_India "Foreign relations of India")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Jawaharlal_Nehru%2C_Nasser_and_Tito_at_the_Conference_of_Non-Aligned_Nations_held_in_Belgrade.jpg/250px-Jawaharlal_Nehru%2C_Nasser_and_Tito_at_the_Conference_of_Non-Aligned_Nations_held_in_Belgrade.jpg)](File:Jawaharlal_Nehru,_Nasser_and_Tito_at_the_Conference_of_Non-Aligned_Nations_held_in_Belgrade.jpg)

In the 1950s and 60s, India played a pivotal role in the [Non-Aligned Movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement "Non-Aligned Movement").[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Dinkel2018-265) From left to right: [Gamal Abdel Nasser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser "Gamal Abdel Nasser") of [United Arab Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Arab_Republic "United Arab Republic") (now Egypt), [Josip Broz Tito](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito "Josip Broz Tito") of [Yugoslavia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia "Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia") and [Jawaharlal Nehru](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru "Jawaharlal Nehru") in Belgrade, September 1961.

India remained a member of the [Commonwealth of Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations "Commonwealth of Nations") after becoming a republic in 1950.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-storm-india-commonwealth-266)[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-267) It strongly supported decolonisation in Africa and Asia in the 1950s, and played a leading role in the Non-Aligned Movement.[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTERothermund200048,_227-268) After cordial relations with China during the greater part of the 1950s, India and China went to [war in 1962](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Indian_War "Sino-Indian War"); India was widely thought to have been decisively defeated.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-62-humiliation-269) By 1967, however, India was able to fend off [Chinese excursions into Sikkim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sino-Indian_War_of_1967 "Sino-Indian War of 1967").[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-270)

India has had [uneasy relations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_relations "Indo-Pakistani relations") with its western neighbour, Pakistan. The two went to war in [1947](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_War_of_1947 "Indo-Pakistani War of 1947"), [1965](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_War_of_1965 "Indo-Pakistani War of 1965"), [1971](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_War_of_1971 "Indo-Pakistani War of 1971"), and [1999](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kargil_War "Kargil War"). Three wars were fought over the [disputed territory of Kashmir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kashmir_conflict "Kashmir conflict").[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGilbert2002486–487-271) After the 1965 war, India began to pursue close military and economic [ties with the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India-Soviet_Union_relations "India-Soviet Union relations"). By the late 1960s, the Soviet Union was India's largest arms supplier.[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESharma199956-272)

China's [nuclear test of 596](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/596_(nuclear_test) "596 (nuclear test)") and threats to intervene in support of Pakistan in the 1965 war caused India to produce nuclear weapons.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerkovich200160–86,_106–125-273) India conducted its [first nuclear weapons test](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smiling_Buddha "Smiling Buddha") in 1974 and carried out [additional underground testing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pokhran-II "Pokhran-II") in 1998. India has signed neither the [Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comprehensive_Nuclear-Test-Ban_Treaty "Comprehensive Nuclear-Test-Ban Treaty") nor the [Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_Non-Proliferation_Treaty "Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty"), considering both to be flawed and discriminatory.[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKumar2010-274) India maintains a "[no first use](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No_first_use "No first use")" nuclear policy and is developing a [nuclear triad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_triad "Nuclear triad") capability as a part of its "[Minimum Credible Deterrence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minimum_Credible_Deterrence "Minimum Credible Deterrence")" doctrine.[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTENair2007-275)[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-276)

Since the end of the [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War"), India has increased its economic, strategic, and military cooperation with the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India–United_States_relations "India–United States relations") and the [European Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India–European_Union_relations "India–European Union relations").[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEuropean_Union_2008-277) In 2008, a [civilian nuclear agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S.–India_Civil_Nuclear_Agreement "U.S.–India Civil Nuclear Agreement") was signed between India and the United States. Although India possessed nuclear weapons at the time and was not a party to the Nuclear Non-Proliferation Treaty, it received waivers from the [International Atomic Energy Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Atomic_Energy_Agency "International Atomic Energy Agency") and the [Nuclear Suppliers Group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_Suppliers_Group "Nuclear Suppliers Group"), ending earlier restrictions on India's nuclear technology and commerce; India subsequently signed co-operation agreements involving [civilian nuclear energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_power_in_India "Nuclear power in India") with Russia,[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBritish_Broadcasting_Corporation_2009-278) France,[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTERediff_2008_a-279) the [United Kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India–United_Kingdom_relations "India–United Kingdom relations"),[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEReuters2010-280) and [Canada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canada–India_relations "Canada–India relations").[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTECurry2010-281)

## Economy

Main article: [Economy of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_India "Economy of India")

The Indian economy has been among the ten [largest in the world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_largest_historical_GDP "List of countries by largest historical GDP") since 2010. As of 2026, India's nominal gross domestic output (GDP) is the [6th largest in the world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal) "List of countries by GDP (nominal)").[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-ID-282)[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-283) Measured by [purchasing power parity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity "Purchasing power parity") (PPP), India is the [third-largest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP) "List of countries by GDP (PPP)") economy.[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-IMFWEO.IN-24) It is one of the [world's fastest-growing economies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_real_GDP_growth_rate "List of countries by real GDP growth rate") with an average annual growth rate exceeding 5% from 1990 to 2010.[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTENayakGoldarAgrawal2010xxv-284)[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEInternational_Monetary_Fund_20112-285) Demographics strain its economy, with the nation historically maintaining [low GDP per capita](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita "List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita") both regionally and as measured by globally.[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-IMFWEO.IN-24) The vast majority of Indians fall into the global low-income group based on average daily income.[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-286)

Until 1991, all Indian governments followed [protectionist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protectionism "Protectionism") policies that were influenced by socialist economics. Widespread [state intervention and regulation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Licence_Raj "Licence Raj") largely walled the economy off from the outside world. An acute [balance of payments crisis in 1991](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Indian_economic_crisis "1991 Indian economic crisis") forced the nation to [liberalise its economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_liberalisation_in_India "Economic liberalisation in India");[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolpert2003xiv-287) since then, it has moved increasingly towards a free-market system[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrganisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development_2007-288)[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGargan1992-289) by emphasising both foreign trade and direct investment inflows.[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAlamgir200823,_97-290) India has been a member of [World Trade Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Trade_Organization "World Trade Organization") since 1 January 1995.[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWorld_Trade_Organization_1995-291)

The 522-million-worker [Indian labour force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labour_in_India "Labour in India") is the [world's second largest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_labour_force "List of countries by labour force"), as of 2017[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=India&action=edit)
Category: ./Category:Articles\_containing\_potentially\_dated\_statements\_from\_2017
Category: ./Category:All\_articles\_containing\_potentially\_dated\_statements
.[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTECentral_Intelligence_Agency-292) The service sector makes up 55.6% of GDP, the industrial sector 26.3% and the agricultural sector 18.1%. India's [foreign exchange remittances](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Remittance "Remittance") of US$100 billion in 2022,[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-293) the highest in the world, were contributed to its economy by 32 million Indians working in foreign countries.[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-294) In 2006, the share of external trade in India's GDP stood at 24%, up from 6% in 1985.[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrganisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development_2007-288) In 2008, India's share of world trade was 1.6%;[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-295) in 2021, it was the [world's ninth-largest importer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_imports "List of countries by imports") and the [sixteenth-largest exporter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_exports "List of countries by exports").[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-296) Between 2001 and 2011, the contribution of petrochemical and engineering goods to total exports grew from 14% to 42%.[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEconomist_2011-297) India was the [world's second-largest textile exporter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_textile_exports "List of countries by textile exports") after [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China") in the 2013 calendar year.[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEconomic_Times_2014-298)

Averaging an economic growth rate of 7.5% for several years before 2007,[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrganisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development_2007-288) India has more than doubled its hourly wage rates during the first decade of the 21st century.[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBonner2010-299) Some 431 million Indians have left poverty since 1985; India's middle classes are projected to number around 580 million by 2030.[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFarrellBeinhocker2007-300) In 2024, India's consumer market was the [world's third largest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_consumer_markets "List of largest consumer markets").[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-301) India's nominal [GDP per capita](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/GDP_per_capita "GDP per capita") increased steadily from US$308 in 1991, when economic liberalisation began, to US$1,380 in 2010, to an estimated US$2,731 in 2024. It is expected to grow to US$3,264 by 2026.[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-IMFWEO.IN-24)

- [![In 2019, 43% of India's total workforce was employed in agriculture.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Plowing_the_land_in_India_-_modern_and_traditional.jpg/330px-Plowing_the_land_in_India_-_modern_and_traditional.jpg)](File:Plowing_the_land_in_India_-_modern_and_traditional.jpg "In 2019, 43% of India's total workforce was employed in agriculture.")

  In 2019, 43% of India's total workforce was employed in agriculture.[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-worldbank-ilo-total-agriculture-302)
- [![A woman growing radish in the foreground and garlic to the right in a village in the Nilgiris, Tamil Nadu. 55% of India's female workforce was employed in agriculture in 2019.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Fields_Akoni_Nilgiris_Tamil_Nadu_Nov24_A7CR_05287.jpg/330px-Fields_Akoni_Nilgiris_Tamil_Nadu_Nov24_A7CR_05287.jpg)](File:Fields_Akoni_Nilgiris_Tamil_Nadu_Nov24_A7CR_05287.jpg "A woman growing radish in the foreground and garlic to the right in a village in the Nilgiris, Tamil Nadu. 55% of India's female workforce was employed in agriculture in 2019.")

  A woman growing radish in the foreground and garlic to the right in a village in the [Nilgiris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nilgiris "Nilgiris"), Tamil Nadu. 55% of India's female workforce was employed in agriculture in 2019.[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-worldbank-ilo-female-agriculture-303)
- [![India is the world's largest producer of milk, with the largest population of cattle. In 2018, nearly 80% of India's milk was sourced from small farms with herd size between one and two, the milk harvested by hand milking.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/ILRI%2C_Stevie_Mann_-_Villager_and_calf_share_milk_from_cow_in_Rajasthan%2C_India.jpg/330px-ILRI%2C_Stevie_Mann_-_Villager_and_calf_share_milk_from_cow_in_Rajasthan%2C_India.jpg)](File:ILRI,_Stevie_Mann_-_Villager_and_calf_share_milk_from_cow_in_Rajasthan,_India.jpg "India is the world's largest producer of milk, with the largest population of cattle. In 2018, nearly 80% of India's milk was sourced from small farms with herd size between one and two, the milk harvested by hand milking.")

  India is the [world's largest producer of milk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_milk_production "List of countries by milk production"), with the largest population of cattle. In 2018, nearly 80% of India's milk was sourced from small farms with herd size between one and two, the milk harvested by hand milking.[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-milk-sourcing-304)

### Industries

Main articles: [Industry in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industry_in_India "Industry in India") and [Energy in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Energy_in_India "Energy in India")

See also: [Energy policy of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Energy_policy_of_India "Energy policy of India")

The [Indian automotive industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_India "Automotive industry in India"), the world's second-fastest growing, increased domestic sales by 26% during 2009–2010,[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBusiness_Line_2010-305) and exports by 36% during 2008–2009.[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEExpress_India_2009-306) In 2022, India became the world's third-largest vehicle market after China and the United States, surpassing Japan.[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-307) At the end of 2011, the [Indian IT industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_technology_in_India "Information technology in India") employed 2.8 million professionals, generated revenues close to US$100 billion equalling 7.5% of Indian GDP, and contributed 26% of India's merchandise exports.[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTENasscom_2011–2012-308)

The [pharmaceutical industry in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pharmaceutical_industry_in_India "Pharmaceutical industry in India") includes 3,000 pharmaceutical companies and 10,500 manufacturing units; India is the world's third-largest pharmaceutical producer, largest producer of generic medicines, and supplies up to 50–60% of global vaccines demand, contributing up to US$24.44 billion in exports. India's local pharmaceutical market is estimated up to US$42 billion.[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Phamra1-309)[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Pharma2-310) India is among the top 12 biotech destinations in the world.[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-311)[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEYep2011-312) The Indian biotech industry grew by 15.1% in 2012–2013, increasing its revenues from ₹204.4 billion ([Indian rupees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_rupee "Indian rupee")) to ₹235.24 billion (US$3.94 billion at June 2013 exchange rates).[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-313)

India's capacity to generate electrical power is 300 gigawatts, of which 42 gigawatts is renewable.[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Par-314) [The country's usage of coal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coal_in_India "Coal in India") is a major cause of [India's greenhouse gas emissions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_in_India#Greenhouse_gas_emissions "Climate change in India"), but [its renewable energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_India "Renewable energy in India") is growing.[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-315) India emits about 7% of global greenhouse gas emissions. This equates to about 2.5 tons of [carbon dioxide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carbon_dioxide "Carbon dioxide") per person per year, which is half the world average.[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-USAID2018-316)[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-UNEP2019-317) Increasing [access to electricity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrification "Electrification") and [clean cooking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clean_cooking "Clean cooking") with [liquefied petroleum gas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liquefied_petroleum_gas "Liquefied petroleum gas") have been priorities for energy in India.[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-318)

- [![Mumbai, the centre of India's tertiary sector finance industry, also contributes to tourism. Shown here are the Taj Mahal Palace Hotel to the left and the Gateway of India.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Panoramic_view_of_Taj_Palace_Hotel_and_Taj_Tower_with_the_iconic_Gateway_of_India_in_the_background.jpg/330px-Panoramic_view_of_Taj_Palace_Hotel_and_Taj_Tower_with_the_iconic_Gateway_of_India_in_the_background.jpg)](File:Panoramic_view_of_Taj_Palace_Hotel_and_Taj_Tower_with_the_iconic_Gateway_of_India_in_the_background.jpg "Mumbai, the centre of India's tertiary sector finance industry, also contributes to tourism. Shown here are the Taj Mahal Palace Hotel to the left and the Gateway of India.")

  [Mumbai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mumbai "Mumbai"), the centre of India's [tertiary sector](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tertiary_sector "Tertiary sector") [finance industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Finance_industry "Finance industry"), also contributes to [tourism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tourism_in_India "Tourism in India"). Shown here are the [Taj Mahal Palace Hotel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taj_Mahal_Palace_Hotel "Taj Mahal Palace Hotel") to the left and the [Gateway of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gateway_of_India "Gateway of India").
- [![A tea garden in Sikkim. India, the world's second-largest producer of tea, is a nation of one billion tea drinkers, who consume 70% of India's tea output.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Cherry_Resort_inside_Temi_Tea_Garden%2C_Namchi%2C_Sikkim.jpg/330px-Cherry_Resort_inside_Temi_Tea_Garden%2C_Namchi%2C_Sikkim.jpg)](File:Cherry_Resort_inside_Temi_Tea_Garden,_Namchi,_Sikkim.jpg "A tea garden in Sikkim. India, the world's second-largest producer of tea, is a nation of one billion tea drinkers, who consume 70% of India's tea output.")

  A tea garden in Sikkim. India, the [world's second-largest producer of tea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_tea_production "List of countries by tea production"), is a nation of one billion tea drinkers, who consume 70% of India's tea output.
- [![A panorama of Bangalore, the centre of India's software development economy. In the 1980s, when the first multinational corporations began to set up centres in India, they chose Bangalore because of the large pool of skilled graduates in the area, in turn due to the many science and engineering colleges in the surrounding region.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Bangalore_Panorama_edit1.jpg/960px-Bangalore_Panorama_edit1.jpg)](File:Bangalore_Panorama_edit1.jpg "A panorama of Bangalore, the centre of India's software development economy.   A panorama of [Bangalore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bangalore "Bangalore"), the centre of India's software development economy. In the 1980s, when the first [multinational corporations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multinational_corporation "Multinational corporation") began to set up centres in India, they chose Bangalore because of the large pool of skilled graduates in the area, in turn due to the many science and engineering colleges in the surrounding region.[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-ScottGarofoli2007-319)
- [![A Chinese fishing net being raised in Kochi. Fishing contributes 1.07% to India's total GDP, and supports over 28 million people, especially within vulnerable communities.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Chinese_Fishing_Net_Raising_Birds_Sunrise_Ashtamudi_Kollam_Mar22_A7C_01784.jpg/330px-Chinese_Fishing_Net_Raising_Birds_Sunrise_Ashtamudi_Kollam_Mar22_A7C_01784.jpg)](File:Chinese_Fishing_Net_Raising_Birds_Sunrise_Ashtamudi_Kollam_Mar22_A7C_01784.jpg "A Chinese fishing net being raised in Kochi. Fishing contributes 1.07% to India's total GDP, and supports over 28 million people, especially within vulnerable communities.")

  A [Chinese fishing net](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_fishing_nets "Chinese fishing nets") being raised in [Kochi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kochi "Kochi"). Fishing contributes 1.07% to India's total [GDP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gross_domestic_product "Gross domestic product"),[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-:2-320) and supports over 28 million people, especially within vulnerable communities.[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-321)

## Demographics

Main article: [Demographics of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demographics_of_India "Demographics of India")

With an estimated 1,428,627,663 residents in 2023, India is the world's most populous country.[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-WPP_UN-322) 1,210,193,422 residents were reported in the [2011 provisional census report](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_Census_of_India "2011 Census of India").[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEProvisional_Population_Totals_Paper_1_of_2011_India160-323) The median age was 28.7 in 2020.[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTECentral_Intelligence_Agency-292) Medical advances made in the last 50 years as well as increased agricultural productivity brought about by the "[Green Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_Revolution_in_India "Green Revolution in India")" have caused India's population to grow rapidly,[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTERorabacher201035–39-324) though India's decennial rates of growth are decreasing: its population grew by 17.64% from 2001 to 2011,[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEProvisional_Population_Totals_Paper_1_of_2011_India165-325) compared to 21.54% growth in the previous decade (1991–2001).[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEProvisional_Population_Totals_Paper_1_of_2011_India165-325) The first post-colonial census, conducted in 1951, counted 361 million people.[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-326) The [life expectancy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_expectancy "Life expectancy") at birth has increased from 49.7 years in 1970–1975 to 72.0 years in 2023.[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-:5-327)[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-328) The under-five [mortality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infant_mortality "Infant mortality") rate for the country was 113 per 1,000 live births in 1994 whereas in 2018 it reduced to 41.1 per 1,000 live births.[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-:5-327)

The human sex ratio, according to the 2011 census, is 940 females per 1,000 males.[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEProvisional_Population_Totals_Paper_1_of_2011_India160-323) [Female infanticide in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Female_infanticide_in_India "Female infanticide in India"), and lately [female foeticide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Female_foeticide_in_India "Female foeticide in India"), have created lop-sided gender ratios; the number of [missing women](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Missing_women "Missing women") in the country quadrupled from 15 million to 63 million during the period 1964–2014, faster than the population growth during the same period.[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-The_Hindu_November_17_2019c-329) According to an Indian government study, an additional 21 million girls are unwanted and do not receive adequate care.[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-The_Guardian_November_17_2019c-330) Despite a government ban on sex-selective foeticide, the practice has far from stopped.[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Foreign_Policy_November_17_2019c-331)

Migration from rural to urban areas has been an important dynamic in India's recent history. The number of people living in urban areas grew by 31.2% between 1991 and 2001.[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGarg2005-332) In 2001, over 70% lived in rural areas.[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDysonVisaria2005115–129-333)[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTERatna2007271–272-334) The level of urbanisation increased further from 27.81% in the 2001 census to 31.16% in the 2011 census. The slowing down of the overall population growth rate was due to the sharp decline in the growth rate in rural areas since 1991.[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandramouli2011-335) In the 2011 census, there were 53 [million-plus urban agglomerations in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_million-plus_urban_agglomerations_in_India "List of million-plus urban agglomerations in India"). Among them [Mumbai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mumbai "Mumbai"), [Delhi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delhi "Delhi"), [Kolkata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kolkata "Kolkata"), [Chennai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chennai "Chennai"), [Bengaluru](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bangalore "Bangalore"), [Hyderabad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyderabad "Hyderabad") and [Ahmedabad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmedabad "Ahmedabad"), in decreasing order by population.[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-censusindia_2011-336)

- [![The historical development of life expectancy in India from 1881 to 2023](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Life-expectancy%2C_1881_to_2023%2C_IND.svg/250px-Life-expectancy%2C_1881_to_2023%2C_IND.svg.png)](File:Life-expectancy,_1881_to_2023,_IND.svg "The historical development of life expectancy in India from 1881 to 2023")

  The historical development of life expectancy in India from 1881 to 2023
- [![The child mortality rate in India from 1960 to 2023](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Child-mortality_rate_in_india.png/330px-Child-mortality_rate_in_india.png)](File:Child-mortality_rate_in_india.png "The child mortality rate in India from 1960 to 2023")

  The child mortality rate in India from 1960 to 2023

### Languages

Main article: [Languages of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Languages_of_India "Languages of India")

Languages of India belong to several [language families](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language_family "Language family"). The [2011 Census of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_Census_of_India "2011 Census of India"), the last conducted by the Indian government, gives the following breakdown:[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-jolad-agarwal-337)

| Language families and speakers in India[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-jolad-agarwal-337) | | | | | |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Serial number | Language family | Sub-family | Number of languages | Number of speakers | Percentage of speakers |
| 1 | [Indo-European](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-European_languages "Indo-European languages") | [Indo-Aryan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages "Indo-Aryan languages") | 21 | 945,052,555 | 78.05% |
| 1 | [Indo-European](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-European_languages "Indo-European languages") | [Iranian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_languages "Iranian languages") | 1 | 21,677 | 0%[[w]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-338) |
| 1 | [Indo-European](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-European_languages "Indo-European languages") | [Germanic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germanic_languages "Germanic languages") | 1 | 259,678 | 0.02% |
| 2 | [Dravidian languages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dravidian_languages "Dravidian languages") |  | 17 | 237,840,116 | 19.64% |
| 3 | [Austro-Asiatic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austro-Asiatic_languages "Austro-Asiatic languages") |  | 14 | 13,493,080 | 1.11% |
| 4 | [Tibeto-Burman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tibeto-Burman_languages "Tibeto-Burman languages") |  | 66 | 12,257,382 | 1.01% |
| 5 | [Semito-Hamitic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afroasiatic_languages "Afroasiatic languages") |  | 1 | 54,947 | 0% |

There are also small numbers of speakers of [Tai–Kadai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kra–Dai_languages "Kra–Dai languages"), [Andamanese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andamanese_languages "Andamanese languages"), and minor language families and [isolates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language_isolate "Language isolate").[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Moseley2008-339): 283

The official language of India's federal government was chosen by the [Constituent Assembly of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constituent_Assembly_of_India "Constituent Assembly of India") in September 1949 after three years of debate between two opposing camps. [Hindi language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindi_language "Hindi language") protagonists wanted Hindi in the [Devanagari script](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Devanagari_script "Devanagari script") to be the sole "national language" of India whereas delegates from South India preferred English to have a place in the Constitution.[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-lerner-Hindi-340)[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-isaka-Hindi-341) The compromise reached declared (i) Hindi to be the "official language" of India's federal government; (ii) English to be an associate official language for 15 years during which Hindi's formal lexicon would be developed; and (iii) the international form of [Hindu–Arabic numerals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu–Arabic_numeral_system "Hindu–Arabic numeral system") to be the official numerals.[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-lerner-Hindi-340)[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-isaka-Hindi-341) The compromise resolution became articles 343–351 of India's constitution, which came into effect on 26 January 1950.[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-lerner-Hindi-340)[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-isaka-Hindi-341) In 1965, after bitter opposition from [South India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_India "South India") to Hindi becoming the sole official language, a compromise was reached to where English would continue to be an "associate official language" indefinitely.[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-342)[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-343)

The [Eighth Schedule of India's Constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eighth_Schedule_to_the_Constitution_of_India "Eighth Schedule to the Constitution of India") also recognises 22 languages, including Hindi but not English, which the government is obligated to develop. These are sometimes called "scheduled languages". This list includes major regional languages, but also others—such as [Sanskrit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanskrit "Sanskrit"), which no longer has [first language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_language "First language") speakers in India, and [Urdu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urdu "Urdu"), which is not region-specific—because of their value to India's cultural heritage.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-KachruKachru2008-1-344)[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-GazzolaWickström2016-345)[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Groff2017-lead-346) In 1950, there were 14 scheduled languages: [Assamese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assamese_language "Assamese language"), [Bengali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bengali_language "Bengali language"), [Gujarati](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gujarati_language "Gujarati language"), [Hindi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindi "Hindi"), [Kannada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kannada "Kannada"), [Kashmiri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kashmiri_language "Kashmiri language"), [Malayalam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malayalam "Malayalam"), [Marathi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marathi_language "Marathi language"), [Oriya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Odia_language "Odia language"), [Punjabi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punjabi_language "Punjabi language"), Sanskrit, [Tamil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamil_language "Tamil language"), [Telugu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Telugu_language "Telugu language") and Urdu.[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-jolad-agarwal-337) In the following decades constitutional amendments added others: [Sindhi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sindhi_language "Sindhi language") (1967), [Nepali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nepali_language "Nepali language"), [Manipuri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meitei_language "Meitei language"), and [Konkani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Konkani_language "Konkani language") (1992), [Maithili](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maithili_language "Maithili language"), [Dogri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dogri_language "Dogri language"), [Santali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santali_language "Santali language") and [Bodo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boro_language_(India) "Boro language (India)") (2004).[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-jolad-agarwal-337)

- [![The regions of first-language speech of the main languages of India](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Language_Map_of_India.jpg/250px-Language_Map_of_India.jpg)](File:Language_Map_of_India.jpg "The regions of first-language speech of the main languages of India")

  The regions of first-language speech of the main languages of India
- [![The main languages of India by relative numbers of speakers](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Indian_Languages_Map.jpg/250px-Indian_Languages_Map.jpg)](File:Indian_Languages_Map.jpg "The main languages of India by relative numbers of speakers")

  The main languages of India by relative numbers of speakers

These are from top to bottom: 1. Assamese, 2. Bengali, 3. Gujarati, 4. Kannada, 5. Kashmiri, 6. Konkani, 7. Malayalam, 8. Marathi, 9. Nepali, 10. Oriya, 11. Punjabi, 12. Sanskrit, 13. Tamil, 14. Telugu, 15. Urdu.")

  On the reverse of each of India's [paper money notes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paper_money "Paper money"), the denomination is listed in a panel on the left in 15 languages, in addition to Hindi and English, which appear more prominently elsewhere. These are from top to bottom: 1. Assamese, 2. Bengali, 3. Gujarati, 4. Kannada, 5. Kashmiri, 6. Konkani, 7. Malayalam, 8. Marathi, 9. Nepali, 10. Oriya, 11. Punjabi, 12. Sanskrit, 13. Tamil, 14. Telugu, 15. Urdu.[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-rupee-15lang-347)

### Religion

Main article: [Religion in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion_in_India "Religion in India")

[Religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion "Religion") in India is characterised by a diversity of beliefs and practices. Throughout India's history, religion has been an important part of its culture. The [Indian subcontinent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_subcontinent "Indian subcontinent") is the birthplace of four [major world religions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_religious_groups "Major religious groups"): [Buddhism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhism "Buddhism"), [Hinduism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hinduism "Hinduism"), [Jainism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jainism "Jainism"), and [Sikhism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sikhism "Sikhism"). India has the largest population of Hindus, Sikhs, and Jains, the third-largest population of Muslims (after [Indonesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indonesia "Indonesia") and [Pakistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakistan "Pakistan")) and the ninth largest of Buddhists.[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Firstpost_Aug2016-348) India also has the largest population of people adhering to both [Zoroastrianism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoroastrianism "Zoroastrianism") ([Parsis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parsi "Parsi") and [Iranis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irani_(India) "Irani (India)")) and the [Bahá'í Faith](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baháʼí_Faith_in_India "Baháʼí Faith in India").[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTESmith200894-349)

The [Preamble to the Constitution of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Preamble_to_the_Constitution_of_India "Preamble to the Constitution of India") declares India to be a [secular state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secular_state "Secular state"),[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-350)[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-351) and [freedom of religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_religion "Freedom of religion") to be a [fundamental right](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fundamental_Rights_in_India "Fundamental Rights in India") ("... liberty of thought, expression, belief, faith, and worship.")[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-352) According to the 2011 census of India, 79.8% of the [population of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demographics_of_India "Demographics of India") follows [Hinduism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hinduism_in_India "Hinduism in India"), 14.2% [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam_in_India "Islam in India"), 2.3% [Christianity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity_in_India "Christianity in India"), 1.7% [Sikhism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sikhism_in_India "Sikhism in India"), 0.7% [Buddhism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhism_in_India "Buddhism in India") and 0.4% [Jainism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jainism_in_India "Jainism in India"). Several tribal religions are also present in India, such as [Donyi-Polo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donyi-Polo "Donyi-Polo"), [Sanamahism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanamahism "Sanamahism"), [Sarnaism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sarnaism "Sarnaism"), and [Niamtre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Niamtre "Niamtre").

- [![Jain pilgrim, Shravanabelagola](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Gomateswara%2C_Shravanabelagola.jpg/120px-Gomateswara%2C_Shravanabelagola.jpg)](File:Gomateswara,_Shravanabelagola.jpg "Jain pilgrim, Shravanabelagola")
