  Interior of the [Magen David Synagogue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magen_David_Synagogue_(Kolkata) "Magen David Synagogue (Kolkata)"), Kolkata

### Education

Main article: [Education in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Education_in_India "Education in India")

See also: [Literacy in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literacy_in_India "Literacy in India") and [History of education in the Indian subcontinent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_education_in_the_Indian_subcontinent "History of education in the Indian subcontinent")

The literacy rate in 2011 was 74.04%: 65.46% among females and 82.14% among males.[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEProvisional_Population_Totals_Paper_1_of_2011_India163-353) The rural-urban literacy gap, which was 21.2 percentage points in 2001, dropped to 16.1 percentage points in 2011. The improvement in the rural literacy rate is twice that of urban areas.[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChandramouli2011-335) In 2011 [Kerala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerala "Kerala") had the highest literary rate, with 93.91% literacy, and [Bihar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bihar "Bihar") the lowest, with 63.82%.[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEProvisional_Population_Totals_Paper_1_of_2011_India163-353) In 1981 the respective literacy rates for total population, men and women were 41%, 53% and 29%. In 1951, the rates were 18%, 27% and 9%. In 1921, the rates 7%, 12% and 2%. In 1891, they were 5%, 9% and 1%.[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-354)[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-355) According to Latika Chaudhary, in 1911 there were under three primary schools for every ten villages. Statistically, more caste and religious diversity reduced private spending. Primary schools taught literacy, so local diversity limited its growth.[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-356)

The education system of India is the world's second-largest.[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-357) India has over 900 universities, 40,000 colleges[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-highered1-358) and 1.5 million schools.[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-359) In India's higher education system, a significant number of seats are reserved under [affirmative action](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reservation_in_India "Reservation in India") policies for the historically disadvantaged. In recent decades India's improved education system is often cited as one of the main contributors to [its economic development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_development_in_India "Economic development in India").[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Sify-360)[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-361)

- [![Children await school lunch in Rayka (also Raika), a village in Gujarat. The salutation Jai Bhim on the blackboard honours the jurist, social reformer, and Dalit leader B. R. Ambedkar.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/47_Raika_School_-_eating_together_%283384824242%29.jpg/250px-47_Raika_School_-_eating_together_%283384824242%29.jpg)](File:47_Raika_School_-_eating_together_(3384824242).jpg "Children await school lunch in Rayka (also Raika), a village in Gujarat. The salutation Jai Bhim on the blackboard honours the jurist, social reformer, and Dalit leader B. R. Ambedkar.")

  Children await school lunch in Rayka (also Raika), a village in Gujarat. The salutation *[Jai Bhim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jai_Bhim "Jai Bhim")* on the blackboard honours the jurist, social reformer, and [Dalit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dalit "Dalit") leader [B. R. Ambedkar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/B._R._Ambedkar "B. R. Ambedkar").
- [![The Madrasah of the Masjid-i-Ala mosque in Srirangapatna, Karnataka, built in the period 1786–87, during the rule of Tipu Sultan](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Madrasah1.jpg/250px-Madrasah1.jpg)](File:Madrasah1.jpg "The Madrasah of the Masjid-i-Ala mosque in Srirangapatna, Karnataka, built in the period 1786–87, during the rule of Tipu Sultan")

  The [Madrasah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madrasah "Madrasah") of the [Masjid-i-Ala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masjid-i-Ala "Masjid-i-Ala") mosque in [Srirangapatna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Srirangapatna "Srirangapatna"), Karnataka, built in the period 1786–87, during the rule of [Tipu Sultan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tipu_Sultan "Tipu Sultan")
- [![IIT Roorkee, formerly the Thomason College of Civil Engineering, is the oldest engineering college in India. It was foundedin 1847 during East India Company rule to train men employed in the construction of the Ganges Canal.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/ThomasonCollegeOfEngineeringRoorkeeEst1847.jpg/250px-ThomasonCollegeOfEngineeringRoorkeeEst1847.jpg)](File:ThomasonCollegeOfEngineeringRoorkeeEst1847.jpg "IIT Roorkee, formerly the Thomason College of Civil Engineering, is the oldest engineering college in India. It was foundedin 1847 during East India Company rule to train men employed in the construction of the Ganges Canal.")

  [IIT Roorkee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IIT_Roorkee "IIT Roorkee"), formerly the Thomason College of Civil Engineering, is the oldest engineering college in India.[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-hedrick-thomason-362)[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-subram-thomason-363) It was foundedin 1847 during [East India Company rule](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Company_rule_in_India "Company rule in India") to train men employed in the construction of the [Ganges Canal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ganges_Canal "Ganges Canal").[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-subram-thomason-363)[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-hedrick-thomason-362)

### Health

Main article: [Health in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Health_in_India "Health in India")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Female_health_workers_in_India_%2834332433890%29.jpg/250px-Female_health_workers_in_India_%2834332433890%29.jpg)](File:Female_health_workers_in_India_(34332433890).jpg)

Immunisation health workers in 2006. Eight years later, and three years after India's last case of polio, the WHO declared India to be polio-free.[[341]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-who-chan-14-feb-2014-364)

India bears a disproportionately large burden of the world's [tuberculosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tuberculosis_in_India "Tuberculosis in India") rates, with [World Health Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Health_Organization "World Health Organization") (WHO) statistics for 2022 estimating 2.8 million new infections annually, accounting for 26% of the global total.[[342]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-365) It is estimated that approximately 40% of the population of India carry [tuberculosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latent_tuberculosis "Latent tuberculosis") infection.[[343]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-366)

In 2018 [chronic obstructive pulmonary disease](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chronic_obstructive_pulmonary_disease "Chronic obstructive pulmonary disease") was the leading cause of death after [heart disease](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heart_disease_in_India "Heart disease in India"). The 10 [most polluted cities in the world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_most-polluted_cities_by_particulate_matter_concentration "List of most-polluted cities by particulate matter concentration") are all in India with more than 140 million people breathing air 10 times or more over the WHO safe limit.
Category: ./Category:All\_articles\_with\_unsourced\_statements
Category: ./Category:Articles\_with\_unsourced\_statements\_from\_June\_2026
[*[citation needed](Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*] As of 2026, air quality reports show that not a single Indian city meets the WHO's safety guidelines.[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-367) In cities like Delhi and Mumbai, breathing the air is equivalent to smoking 30 cigarettes a day.
Category: ./Category:All\_articles\_with\_unsourced\_statements
Category: ./Category:Articles\_with\_unsourced\_statements\_from\_June\_2026
[*[citation needed](Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*] In 2017, air pollution killed 1.24 million Indians.[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-368)

## Culture

Main article: [Culture of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_of_India "Culture of India")

### Society

Main articles: [Caste system in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caste_system_in_India "Caste system in India") and [Gender inequality in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_inequality_in_India "Gender inequality in India")

Although sometimes applied to other cultures and religions, caste is a uniquely Indian, and Hindu, social institution.[[x]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-370) All Hindus fall broadly into four castes, or *[varnas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Varna_(Hinduism) "Varna (Hinduism)")*: [Brahmin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brahmin "Brahmin"), or priests, at the top; below them [Kshatriya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kshatriya "Kshatriya"), or warriors; further below, [Vaishya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vaishya "Vaishya"), or merchants and farmers; and at the bottom, [Shudra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shudra "Shudra"), or the service class. Outside the caste system, and therefore of traditional Hinduism, lie people formerly called "outcastes" or "untouchables," and now [scheduled caste](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scheduled_caste "Scheduled caste") (a term used in India's constitution) or [Dalit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dalit "Dalit"), a later self-description of pride, meaning "broken" or "downtrodden". Each caste is further divided into sub-castes, or [jatis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jāti "Jāti"), many of which are tied to occupations. The custom of [endogamy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endogamy "Endogamy"), or marrying within one's subcaste, however, makes caste a hereditary label, not of one occupational choice, and has caused the caste system, therefore, to become entrenched.[[347]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-atrey1-371) The [Constituent Assembly of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constituent_Assembly_of_India "Constituent Assembly of India") abolished untouchability in 1947,[[348]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-nyt-india-constit-assmb-caste-372) the [Republic of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_India "Republic of India") did more formally in 1950, and India has since enacted other anti-discriminatory laws and social welfare initiatives related to caste. Still, caste-based inequality, discrimination, segregation, and [violence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caste-related_violence_in_India "Caste-related violence in India") persist.[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-373)[[350]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-374)

Multi-generational [patrilineal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patrilineal "Patrilineal") [joint families](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_family "Joint family") have been the norm in India, though [nuclear families](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_family "Nuclear family") are becoming common in urban areas.[[351]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMakar2007-375) A very large majority of Indians have [their marriages arranged](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arranged_marriage_in_the_Indian_subcontinent "Arranged marriage in the Indian subcontinent") by their parents or family elders.[[352]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMedora2003-376) Marriage is thought to be for life;[[352]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMedora2003-376) and the divorce rate is extremely low;[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJonesRamdas2005111-377) less than one in a thousand marriages end in divorce.[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-378) Many women marry before reaching 18, which is their legal marriageable age; [child marriages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Child_marriage "Child marriage") are not uncommon, especially in rural areas.[[355]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTECullen-Dupont200996-379) In large parts of Hindu northern India, moreover, a form of territorial [exogamy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exogamy "Exogamy") is observed in which a bride marries out of her natal village and her parents do not visit her in her married home; the annual rite [raksha bandhan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raksha_bandhan "Raksha bandhan"), during which married women return to their [natal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Birth "Birth") homes, has served both to affirm bonds with their natal families and offer a recourse in times of marital stress.[[356]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Agarwal1994-380)[[357]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Coleman2017-381)

- [![A Gond tribe member during the Dandari festival in Jainoor, Telangana. The Gond religion predates the Hindu synthesis of the mid-first-millennium BCE.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Closeup_at_Gussadi_dance_performer.jpg/330px-Closeup_at_Gussadi_dance_performer.jpg)](File:Closeup_at_Gussadi_dance_performer.jpg "A Gond tribe member during the Dandari festival in Jainoor, Telangana. The Gond religion predates the Hindu synthesis of the mid-first-millennium BCE.")

  A [Gond](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gondi_people "Gondi people") tribe member during the [Dandari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gussadi_dance "Gussadi dance") festival in [Jainoor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jainoor "Jainoor"), Telangana. The Gond religion predates the [Hindu synthesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindu_synthesis "Hindu synthesis") of the mid-first-millennium BCE.
- [![A member of the Ramnami Samaj, a movement among Dalits, whose members worship the Hindu deity Rama and tattoo their bodies with his name](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/A_smiling_member_of_the_Ramnami_Samaj_%28edited%29.jpg/330px-A_smiling_member_of_the_Ramnami_Samaj_%28edited%29.jpg)](File:A_smiling_member_of_the_Ramnami_Samaj_(edited).jpg "A member of the Ramnami Samaj, a movement among Dalits, whose members worship the Hindu deity Rama and tattoo their bodies with his name")

  A member of the [Ramnami Samaj](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramnami_Samaj "Ramnami Samaj"), a movement among [Dalits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dalit "Dalit"), whose members worship the Hindu deity [Rama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rama "Rama") and tattoo their bodies with his name
- [![A Hindu bride in Ahmedabad, Gujarat](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Hindu_Bride%2C_Ahmedabad%2C_Gujarat.jpg/250px-Hindu_Bride%2C_Ahmedabad%2C_Gujarat.jpg)](File:Hindu_Bride,_Ahmedabad,_Gujarat.jpg "A Hindu bride in Ahmedabad, Gujarat")

  A Hindu bride in [Ahmedabad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmedabad "Ahmedabad"), Gujarat

### Visual art

Main article: [Indian art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_art "Indian art")

India has a very ancient tradition of art, which has exchanged many influences with the rest of [Eurasia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasia "Eurasia"), especially in the first millennium. During this period [Buddhist art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhist_art "Buddhist art") spread with Indian religions to [Central](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia "Central Asia"), [East](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Asia "East Asia") and [Southeast Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeast_Asia "Southeast Asia"), the last also greatly influenced by Hindu art.[[358]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTERowland1970185–198,_252,_385–466-382) Thousands of [seals from the Indus Valley civilisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indus_Valley_civilisation#Seals "Indus Valley civilisation") of the third millennium BCE have been found, usually carved with animals, but also some with human figures. The [Pashupati seal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pashupati_seal "Pashupati seal"), excavated in [Mohenjo-daro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohenjo-daro "Mohenjo-daro"), Pakistan, in 1928–29, is the best known.[[359]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraven199714–16-383)[[360]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarle199417–18-384) Virtually no art survives from a long period following the Indus Valley Civilisation.[[360]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarle199417–18-384)[[361]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTERowland197046–47-385) Almost all surviving ancient Indian art thereafter is in various forms of religious [sculpture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_sculpture "Indian sculpture") in durable materials, or coins. There was probably originally far more in wood, which is lost. In north India [Mauryan art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mauryan_art "Mauryan art") is the first imperial movement.[[362]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraven199735–46-386)[[363]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTERowland197067–70-387)[[364]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarle199422–24-388)

Over the following centuries a distinctly Indian style of sculpting the human figure developed, with less interest in articulating precise anatomy than [ancient Greek sculpture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek_sculpture "Ancient Greek sculpture") but showing smoothly flowing forms expressing *prana* ("breath" or life-force).[[365]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraven199722,_88-389)[[366]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTERowland197035,_99–100-390) This is often complicated by the need to give figures multiple arms or heads, or represent different genders on the left and right of figures, as with the [Ardhanarishvara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ardhanarishvara "Ardhanarishvara") form of Shiva and [Parvati](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parvati "Parvati").[[367]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraven199718–19-391)[[368]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlurton1993151-392)

Most of the earliest large sculpture is Buddhist, either excavated from Buddhist [stupas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stupa "Stupa") such as [Sanchi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanchi "Sanchi"), [Sarnath](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sarnath "Sarnath") and [Amaravati](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amaravati_Stupa "Amaravati Stupa"),[[369]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarle199432–38-393) or is rock cut [reliefs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Relief "Relief") at sites such as [Ajanta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ajanta_Caves "Ajanta Caves"), [Karla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karla_Caves "Karla Caves") and [Ellora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ellora "Ellora"). Hindu and Jain sites appear rather later.[[370]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarle199443–55-394)[[371]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTERowland1970113–119-395) In spite of this complex mixture of religious traditions, generally, the prevailing artistic style at any time and place has been shared by the major religious groups, and sculptors probably usually served all communities.[[372]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlurton199310–11-396) [Gupta art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gupta_art "Gupta art"), at its peak c. 300 CE – c. 500 CE, is often regarded as a classical period whose influence lingered for many centuries after; it saw a new dominance of Hindu sculpture, as at the [Elephanta Caves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elephanta_Caves "Elephanta Caves").[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraven1997111–121-397)[[374]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMichell200044–70-398) Across the north, this became rather stiff and formulaic after c. 800 CE, though rich with finely carved detail in the surrounds of statues.[[375]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarle1994212–216-399) But in the South, under the [Pallava](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pallava_dynasty "Pallava dynasty") and [Chola dynasties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chola_dynasty "Chola dynasty"), sculpture in both stone and bronze had a [sustained period of great achievement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chola_art_and_architecture#Sculpture_and_bronzes "Chola art and architecture"); the large bronzes with Shiva as [Nataraja](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nataraja "Nataraja") have become an iconic symbol of India.[[376]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraven1997152–160-400)[[377]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlurton1993225–227-401)

Ancient paintings have only survived at a few sites, of which the crowded scenes of court life in the [Ajanta Caves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ajanta_Caves "Ajanta Caves") are some of the most important.[[378]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarle1994356–361-402)[[379]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTERowland1970242–251-403) Painted manuscripts of religious texts survive from Eastern India from 10th century onwards, most of the earliest being Buddhist and later Jain. These significantly influenced later artistic styles.[[380]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarle1994361–370-404) The Persian-derived [Deccan painting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deccan_painting "Deccan painting"), starting just before the [Mughal miniature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mughal_miniature "Mughal miniature"), between them give the first large body of secular painting, with an emphasis on portraits, and the recording of princely pleasures and wars.[[381]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraven1997202–208-405)[[382]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarle1994372–382,_400–406-406) The style spread to Hindu courts, especially [among the Rajputs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rajput_painting "Rajput painting"), and developed a variety of styles, with the smaller courts often the most innovative, with figures such as [Nihâl Chand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nihâl_Chand "Nihâl Chand") and [Nainsukh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nainsukh "Nainsukh").[[383]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraven1997222–243-407)[[384]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarle1994384–397,_407–420-408) As a market developed among European residents, it was supplied by [Company painting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Company_painting "Company painting") by Indian artists with considerable Western influence.[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraven1997243-409)[[386]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMichell2000210-410) In the 19th century, cheap [Kalighat paintings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kalighat_painting "Kalighat painting") of gods and everyday life, done on paper, were urban [folk art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folk_art "Folk art") from [Calcutta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calcutta "Calcutta"), which later saw the [Bengal School of Art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bengal_School_of_Art "Bengal School of Art"), reflecting the art colleges founded by the British, the first movement in [modern Indian painting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_Indian_painting "Modern Indian painting").[[387]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMichell2000210–211-411)[[388]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBlurton1993211-412)

- [![Gupta terracotta relief, Krishna Killing the Horse Demon Keshi, 5th century](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/MET_DT5237_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-MET_DT5237_%28cropped%29.jpg)](File:MET_DT5237_(cropped).jpg "Gupta terracotta relief, Krishna Killing the Horse Demon Keshi, 5th century")

  [Chola bronze](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chola_art_and_architecture#Sculpture_and_bronzes "Chola art and architecture") of [Shiva](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shiva "Shiva") as [Nataraja](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nataraja "Nataraja") ("Lord of Dance"), [Tamil Nadu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamil_Nadu "Tamil Nadu"), 10th or 11th century

### Mathematics

Main articles: [Indian mathematics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_mathematics "Indian mathematics") and [Kerala school of astronomy and mathematics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerala_school_of_astronomy_and_mathematics "Kerala school of astronomy and mathematics")

Significant mathematics began in India in the first millennium BCE. The *[Śulba Sūtras](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shulba_Sutras "Shulba Sutras")* (literally, "Aphorisms of the Chords" in [Vedic Sanskrit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vedic_Sanskrit "Vedic Sanskrit")) (c. 700–400 BCE) contain the earliest extant verbal expression of the [Pythagorean theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pythagorean_theorem "Pythagorean theorem") (although very likely it had been known to the [Old Babylonians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Babylonian_dynasty "First Babylonian dynasty").)[[389]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-hayashi2005-p363-413)[[y]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-416) All mathematical works were orally transmitted until approximately 500 BCE; thereafter, they were transmitted both orally and in manuscript form. The oldest extant mathematical document produced on the Indian subcontinent is the birch bark [Bakhshali manuscript](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bakhshali_manuscript "Bakhshali manuscript") from the 7th century CE.[[392]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-hayashi95-417)[[393]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-plofker-brit6-418)

In the classical period of Indian mathematics (400 CE to 1200 CE), important contributions were made by [Aryabhata](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aryabhata "Aryabhata"), [Brahmagupta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brahmagupta "Brahmagupta"), [Bhaskara II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bhaskara_II "Bhaskara II"), [Varāhamihira](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Varāhamihira "Varāhamihira"), and [Madhava](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madhava_of_Sangamagrama "Madhava of Sangamagrama"). The [decimal number system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decimal "Decimal") in use today[[394]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-irfah346-419) was first recorded in Indian mathematics.[[395]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-420) Indian mathematicians made early contributions to the study of the concept of [zero](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/0_(number) "0 (number)") as a number,[[396]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-bourbaki46-421) [negative numbers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negative_numbers "Negative numbers"),[[397]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-bourbaki49-422) [arithmetic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arithmetic "Arithmetic"), and [algebra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algebra "Algebra").[[398]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-concise-britannica-423) [Trigonometry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trigonometry "Trigonometry")[[399]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-424) was further advanced in India, and the modern definitions of [sine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sine "Sine") and [cosine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosine "Cosine") were developed there.[[400]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-425) These mathematical concepts were transmitted to the Middle East, China, and Europe.[[398]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-concise-britannica-423) A later landmark in Indian mathematics was the development of the [series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Series_(mathematics) "Series (mathematics)") expansions for [trigonometric functions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trigonometric_function "Trigonometric function") (sine, cosine, and [arc tangent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arc_tangent "Arc tangent")) by mathematicians of the [Kerala school](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerala_school_of_astronomy_and_mathematics "Kerala school of astronomy and mathematics") in the 15th century CE. Their work, completed two centuries before the invention of [calculus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calculus "Calculus") in Europe, provided the first example of a [power series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_series "Power series").[[z]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-426)[[401]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-427) In the modern era [Srinivasa Ramanujan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Srinivasa_Ramanujan "Srinivasa Ramanujan") made fundamental contributions to [number theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Number_theory "Number theory").[[402]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-hardy-ramanumajan-notice-428)

### Music

Main article: [Music of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music_of_India "Music of India")

India contains a wide array of musical practices, including many different [folk musics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_folk_music "Indian folk music") from different regions. [Indian classical music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_classical_music "Indian classical music") has Vedic origins, and split in the 13th century into the two main traditions of [Hindustani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindustani_classical_music "Hindustani classical music") and [Carnatic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnatic_music "Carnatic music") music. Hindustani is associated with North India and is more [improvisational](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Musical_improvisation "Musical improvisation"), featuring instruments such as the [sitar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sitar "Sitar") and [tabla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tabla "Tabla"), and Carnatic is South Indian and more focused on written [compositions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Musical_composition "Musical composition") such as the *[kriti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kriti_(music) "Kriti (music)")*, while both styles contain common elements such as the [raga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raga "Raga") melodic framework and [tala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tala_(music) "Tala (music)") rhythmic meter.[[403]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-429) Indian music has influenced western genres, including [rock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rock_music "Rock music") and [jazz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jazz "Jazz") musicians during the [1960s counterculture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counterculture_of_the_1960s "Counterculture of the 1960s").[[404]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-430)

[Indian film music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_film_music "Indian film music") is music written for [Indian cinema](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cinema_of_India "Cinema of India"), generally composed by [music directors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Indian_film_music_directors "List of Indian film music directors") and sung by [playback singers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Playback_singers "Playback singers"). Modern [Indian pop](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_pop "Indian pop") takes influences from classical, folk, and western pop music.[[405]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-431)

- [![M. S. Subbulakshmi, Carnatic music vocalist](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Sakunthala_1940_filmposter_%282%29.jpg/120px-Sakunthala_1940_filmposter_%282%29.jpg)](File:Sakunthala_1940_filmposter_(2).jpg "M. S. Subbulakshmi, Carnatic music vocalist")

Shankar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/L._Shankar "L. Shankar").

### Dance

Main article: [Dance in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dance_in_India "Dance in India")

Dance in India has drawn heavily from [Indian classical dance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_classical_dance "Indian classical dance") traditions. Many of these in turn arose in temples or other religious contexts. Their sponsorship and promotion, however, has continued in secular, modern India.[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-vatsyayan-lord-432)[[aa]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-433) India also has local and modern dance traditions.[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-vatsyayan-lord-432) Whether a dance is classical is determined by the [Sangeet Natak Academi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sangeet_Natak_Academi "Sangeet Natak Academi"), the Indian government's organisation for performing arts.[[ab]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-434) Although more dances could perhaps meet the criteria for classical, the Akademi has chosen eight.[[ac]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-435)

Classical Dances of India[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-vatsyayan-lord-432)[[407]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-436)

| Serial number | Dance | Indigenous to: State | Region | Type or origin | Musical accompaniment |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | [Bharatanatyam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bharatanatyam "Bharatanatyam") | [Tamil Nadu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamil_Nadu "Tamil Nadu") | [South India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_India "South India") | Temple dance | [Cinna Melam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melam "Melam"), [Carnatic music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnatic_music "Carnatic music") |
| 2 | [Kathak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kathak "Kathak") | [Uttar Pradesh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh "Uttar Pradesh") | [North India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_India "North India") | [Court dance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Court_dance "Court dance") | [Hindustani music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindustani_music "Hindustani music") |
| 3 | [Kathakali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kathakali "Kathakali") | [Kerala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerala "Kerala") | South India | Dance-drama | [Madhalam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madhalam "Madhalam") drum ensembles; [Sopana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sopana_Sangeetham "Sopana Sangeetham") vocal music |
| 4 | [Kuchipudi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuchipudi "Kuchipudi") | [Andhra Pradesh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh "Andhra Pradesh") | South India | Dance-drama | Carnatic music ensemble |
| 5 | [Manipuri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manipuri_dance "Manipuri dance") | [Manipur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manipur "Manipur") | [Northeast India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northeast_India "Northeast India") | Temple/ritual dance | Ensemble comprising [Pung Cholom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pung_Cholom "Pung Cholom"), flutes, trumpets, [Tambura](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanbur "Tanbur"), [Pena](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pena_(musical_instrument) "Pena (musical instrument)"), and cymbals |
| 6 | [Mohiniattam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohiniattam "Mohiniattam") | Kerala | South India | Dance-drama | Carnatic ensemble |
| 7 | [Odissi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Odissi "Odissi") | [Odisha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Odisha "Odisha") | [East India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_India "East India") | Temple dance | Ensemble of Hindustani music instruments: [pakhavaj](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pakhavaj "Pakhavaj"), [sitar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sitar "Sitar"), flute, cymbals, [harmonium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harmonium "Harmonium") |
| 8 | [Sattriya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sattriya "Sattriya") | [Assam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assam "Assam") | Northeast India | Dance-drama | [Borgeet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Borgeet "Borgeet") accompanied by [khol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khol "Khol") drums and cymbals. |

The best-known classical dance is Bharatnatyam, which began in the temple dances of [Tamil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamil_people "Tamil people") [devadasis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Devadasi "Devadasi").[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-vatsyayan-lord-432) Identified with "prostitutes and courtesans", their dancing was formally banned in 1947.[[ad]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-437) Concurrently, the dance was rehabilitated as a "pure" art form, with [Rukmini Devi Arundale](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rukmini_Devi_Arundale "Rukmini Devi Arundale") as a prominent figure. A devdasi who went on to attain national and international prominence was [Thanjavur Balasaraswati](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balasaraswati "Balasaraswati").[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-vatsyayan-lord-432) Some sources consider the dance-dramas [Chhau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chhau_dance "Chhau dance") of [Jharkhand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jharkhand "Jharkhand"), [West Bengal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Bengal "West Bengal"), and [Odisha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Odisha "Odisha") and [Yakshagana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yakshagana "Yakshagana") of [Karnataka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karnataka "Karnataka") to also belong to the classical tradition.[[408]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-burch-2013-438)

Local dance traditions vary widely across India. In addition to the dance-dramas Chhau and Yakshagana, they include dance-dramas [Raslila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raslila "Raslila") of western [Uttar Pradesh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh "Uttar Pradesh") and [Terukkuttu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Terukkuttu "Terukkuttu") of Tamil Nadu; calendrical and festival dances such as the [Bhangra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bhangra_(dance) "Bhangra (dance)") of Punjab, especially at [Vaisakhi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vaisakhi "Vaisakhi"), the onset of spring, and [Garba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Garba_(dance) "Garba (dance)") of [Gujarat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gujarat "Gujarat") during [Navratri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Navratri "Navratri"); and tribal or [Adivasi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adivasi "Adivasi") dances, such as those of the [Santal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santal "Santal") and [Toda people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toda_people "Toda people"), the latter, for example, in honour of the god [Ön](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toda_people#Religion "Toda people") who brought buffalo to earth.[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-vatsyayan-lord-432)

Among 20th-century directions is the [modern dance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_dance "Modern dance") of [Uday Shankar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uday_Shankar "Uday Shankar") in which classical styles were employed but not adhered to rigidly. Examples are dance-dramas based on the ancient Indian [animal fables](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal_fable "Animal fable"), *[Panchatantra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panchatantra "Panchatantra")*, and Nehru's mid-century meditation on Indian history, *[The Discovery of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Discovery_of_India "The Discovery of India")*.[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-vatsyayan-lord-432) Dance has been an essential aspect of Indian films from the first [talkies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talkies "Talkies") of the 1930s. The individual and group dances of [Bollywood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bollywood "Bollywood"), for example, show a broad range of influences, including classical, local, and Western popular dance.[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-vatsyayan-lord-432) Towards the end of the 20th century, innovations in [British South Asian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_South_Asian "British South Asian") music and dance, such as [Post-Bhangra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music_of_the_United_Kingdom_(1990s)#Post-Bhangra "Music of the United Kingdom (1990s)"), fed back into dance in India.[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-vatsyayan-lord-432)

- [![The Kathakali dance of Kerala](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Kathakali_of_Kerala_at_Nishagandhi_dance_festival_2024_%28266%29.jpg/330px-Kathakali_of_Kerala_at_Nishagandhi_dance_festival_2024_%28266%29.jpg)](File:Kathakali_of_Kerala_at_Nishagandhi_dance_festival_2024_(266).jpg "The Kathakali dance of Kerala")

  The *Kathakali* dance of [Kerala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kerala "Kerala")
- [![The Bharatanatyam dance of Tamil Nadu](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Bharata_Natyam_Performance_DS.jpg/120px-Bharata_Natyam_Performance_DS.jpg)](File:Bharata_Natyam_Performance_DS.jpg "The Bharatanatyam dance of Tamil Nadu")

  The *Bharatanatyam* dance of [Tamil Nadu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamil_Nadu "Tamil Nadu")
- [![The Kathak dance of northern India absorbed Persian and Central Asian influences during Mughal rule.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Kathak_Solo_Performance_%288%29.jpg/330px-Kathak_Solo_Performance_%288%29.jpg)](File:Kathak_Solo_Performance_(8).jpg "The Kathak dance of northern India absorbed Persian and Central Asian influences during Mughal rule.")

  The *Kathak* dance of northern India absorbed Persian and Central Asian influences during [Mughal rule](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mughal_Empire "Mughal Empire").

### Clothing

Main article: [Clothing in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clothing_in_India "Clothing in India")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/India_School.jpg/250px-India_School.jpg)](File:India_School.jpg)

Women in [sari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sari "Sari") at an adult literacy class in [Tamil Nadu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tamil_Nadu "Tamil Nadu")

From ancient times until the advent of the modern, the most widely worn traditional dress in India was [draped](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Draped_garment "Draped garment").[[409]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Tarlo1996-26-439) For women it took the form of a [sari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sari "Sari"), a single piece of cloth many yards long.[[409]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Tarlo1996-26-439) The sari was traditionally wrapped around the lower body and the shoulder.[[409]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Tarlo1996-26-439) In its modern form, it is combined with an underskirt, or Indian [petticoat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petticoat#Asian_petticoats "Petticoat"), and tucked in along the waist band for more secure fastening. It is also commonly worn with an Indian [blouse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blouse "Blouse"), or [choli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Choli "Choli"), which serves as the primary upper-body garment, the sari's end—passing over the shoulder—covering the midriff and obscuring the upper body's contours.[[409]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Tarlo1996-26-439) For men, a similar but shorter length of cloth, the [dhoti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dhoti "Dhoti"), has served as a lower-body garment.[[410]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Tarlo1996-26-28-440)

The use of stitched clothes became widespread after Muslim rule was established by the [Delhi sultanate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delhi_sultanate "Delhi sultanate") (c. 1300 CE) and continued by the [Mughal Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mughal_Empire "Mughal Empire") (c. 1525 CE).[[411]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Rahman-Alkazi2002-441) Among the garments introduced during this time and still commonly worn are: the [shalwars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shalwar_kameez "Shalwar kameez") and [pyjamas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pyjama "Pyjama"), both styles of trousers, and the tunics [kurta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kurta "Kurta") and [kameez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kameez "Kameez").[[411]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Rahman-Alkazi2002-441) Shalwars are atypically wide at the waist but narrow to a cuffed bottom. They are held up by a drawstring, which causes them to become pleated around the waist.[[412]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-StevensonWaite2011-442) When the pants are cut quite narrow, on the [bias](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grain_(textile)#Bias "Grain (textile)"), they are called [churidars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Churidar "Churidar"). The kameez is a long shirt or tunic.[[413]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-StevensonWaite2011-b-443) Its side seams left open below the waistline.[[414]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-444) The kurta is traditionally collarless and made of cotton or silk; it is worn plain or with embroidered decoration, such as [chikankari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chikankari "Chikankari"); and typically falls to either just above or just below the wearer's knees.[[415]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Shukla2015-445)

In the last 50 years, fashions have changed a great deal in India. Increasingly, in urban northern India, the sari is no longer the apparel of everyday wear, though they remain popular on formal occasions. The traditional shalwar kameez is rarely worn by younger urban women, who favour churidars or jeans. In office settings, ubiquitous air conditioning allows men to wear sports jackets year-round. For weddings and formal occasions, men in the middle and upper classes often wear bandhgala, or short [Nehru jackets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nehru_jackets "Nehru jackets"), with pants, with the groom and his [groomsmen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Groomsmen "Groomsmen") sporting [sherwanis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sherwani "Sherwani") and churidars.[[416]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Dwyer2014-446)

- [![A man in dhoti and woollen shawl in Varanasi](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Water_pump%2C_Varanasi_%2815563170660%29_Cropped.jpg/120px-Water_pump%2C_Varanasi_%2815563170660%29_Cropped.jpg)](File:Water_pump,_Varanasi_(15563170660)_Cropped.jpg "A man in dhoti and woollen shawl in Varanasi")

  A man in [dhoti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dhoti "Dhoti") and woollen shawl in [Varanasi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Varanasi "Varanasi")
- [![Female tourists from Manipur in shawl and phanek—lower-body garment similar to a sarong](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/GroupFromNorthEastIndiaAtTaj.jpg/250px-GroupFromNorthEastIndiaAtTaj.jpg)](File:GroupFromNorthEastIndiaAtTaj.jpg "Female tourists from Manipur in shawl and phanek—lower-body garment similar to a sarong")

  Female tourists from [Manipur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manipur "Manipur") in shawl and [phanek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phanek "Phanek")—lower-body garment similar to a [sarong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sarong "Sarong")[[417]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-phanek-447)
- [![Women in shalwar-kameez in Puducherry](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Women_of_Puducherry.jpg/250px-Women_of_Puducherry.jpg)](File:Women_of_Puducherry.jpg "Women in shalwar-kameez in Puducherry")

  Women in [shalwar-kameez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shalwar-kameez "Shalwar-kameez") in [Puducherry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puducherry_(union_territory) "Puducherry (union territory)")

### Cuisine

Main article: [Indian cuisine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_cuisine "Indian cuisine")

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Making_Khameeri_Roti_in_Tandoor_in_Turkman_Gate_Old_Delhi.webm/250px--Making_Khameeri_Roti_in_Tandoor_in_Turkman_Gate_Old_Delhi.webm.jpg)](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/81/Making_Khameeri_Roti_in_Tandoor_in_Turkman_Gate_Old_Delhi.webm)

A tandoor chef in [Turkman Gate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkman_Gate "Turkman Gate"), [Old Delhi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_Delhi "Old Delhi"), makes *khameri roti*, a Muslim-influenced style of [leavened bread](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bread#Leavening "Bread").[[ae]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-449)[[419]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Panjabi1995-450)

The foundation of a typical Indian meal is a cereal cooked plainly and complemented with savoury dishes.[[420]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Davidson2014-p409-451) The cooked cereal could be steamed rice; [chapati](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chapati "Chapati"), a thin unleavened bread;[[421]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Davidson2014-p161-452) [idli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Idli "Idli"), a steamed breakfast cake; or [dosa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dosa_(food) "Dosa (food)"), a griddled pancake.[[422]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-tamang-yeast-idlidosa-453) The savoury dishes might include [lentils](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lentil "Lentil"), [pulses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pulses "Pulses"), vegetables, meat, poultry and fish commonly spiced with [ginger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ginger_root "Ginger root") and [garlic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Garlic "Garlic"), but also [coriander](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coriander "Coriander"), [cumin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cumin "Cumin"), [turmeric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turmeric "Turmeric"), [cinnamon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cinnamon "Cinnamon"), [cardamom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cardamom "Cardamom") and others.[[420]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Davidson2014-p409-451) In some instances, the ingredients may be mixed during the cooking process.[[423]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-jhala-princely-biryani-454) India has distinctive vegetarian cuisines, each a feature of the geographical and cultural histories of its adherents.[[424]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Davidson2014-p410-455) About 20% to 39% of India's population consists of vegetarians.[[425]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-456)[[426]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-457) Although meat is eaten widely, the proportional consumption of meat is low.[[427]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-SahakianSaloma2016-50-458)

The most significant import of cooking techniques into India during the last millennium occurred during the [Mughal Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mughal_Empire "Mughal Empire"), spreading into northern India from regions to its northwest,[[428]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-CollinghamCollingham2007-459) along with dishes such as [pilaf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pilaf "Pilaf").[[429]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoger2000-460)[[430]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-sengupta-74-461) Onions, garlic, almonds, and spices were added to the simple yogurt marinade of Persia.[[428]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-CollinghamCollingham2007-459) Rice was partially cooked and layered alternately with sauteed meat, the pot sealed tightly, and slow cooked according to another Persian cooking technique, to produce [biryani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biryani "Biryani"),[[428]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-CollinghamCollingham2007-459) a feature of festive dining in many parts of India.[[431]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-nandy2004-462)

The diversity of Indian food served worldwide has been partially concealed by the dominance of [Punjabi cuisine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punjabi_cuisine "Punjabi cuisine"). The popularity of [tandoori chicken](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tandoori_chicken "Tandoori chicken")—cooked in a [tandoor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tandoor "Tandoor") oven, which had traditionally been used for baking bread in the rural Punjab and the Delhi region, especially among Muslims, but which is originally from [Central Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia "Central Asia")—dates to the 1950s, and was caused in large part by an entrepreneurial response among people from the Punjab who had been displaced by the 1947 partition.[[424]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Davidson2014-p410-455)

- [![South Indian vegetarian thali, or platter](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/South_Indian_Thali_Cropped.jpg/330px-South_Indian_Thali_Cropped.jpg)](File:South_Indian_Thali_Cropped.jpg "South Indian vegetarian thali, or platter")

  South Indian vegetarian [thali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thali "Thali"), or platter
- [![Machher jhol, a spicy fish curry eaten in eastern India, Nepal, and Bangladesh](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Pabda_Jhaal_-_Home-_Kolkata_-_West_Bengal.jpg/330px-Pabda_Jhaal_-_Home-_Kolkata_-_West_Bengal.jpg)](File:Pabda_Jhaal_-_Home-_Kolkata_-_West_Bengal.jpg "Machher jhol, a spicy fish curry eaten in eastern India, Nepal, and Bangladesh")

  [Machher jhol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machher_jhol "Machher jhol"), a spicy fish curry eaten in eastern India, Nepal, and Bangladesh
- [![Mango, the national fruit of India, is eaten widely in the summer months.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Khairdeen%2C_alias_Pritam%2C_relishing_a_mango_at_the_dusk_of_his_life_05.jpg/330px-Khairdeen%2C_alias_Pritam%2C_relishing_a_mango_at_the_dusk_of_his_life_05.jpg)](File:Khairdeen,_alias_Pritam,_relishing_a_mango_at_the_dusk_of_his_life_05.jpg "Mango, the national fruit of India, is eaten widely in the summer months.")

  [Mango](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mango "Mango"), the national fruit of India, is eaten widely in the summer months.[[432]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-mango-national-fruit-463)[[af]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-466)

### Sports

Main article: [Sport in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sport_in_India "Sport in India")

Several traditional indigenous sports such as *[kabaddi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kabaddi "Kabaddi")*, *[kho kho](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kho_kho "Kho kho")*, *[pehlwani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pehlwani "Pehlwani")* and *[gilli-danda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilli-danda "Gilli-danda")*, and also [martial arts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_martial_arts "Indian martial arts"), such as *[Kalarippayattu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kalarippayattu "Kalarippayattu")* and *[marma adi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marma_adi "Marma adi")* remain popular. [Chess](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chess "Chess") is commonly held to have [originated in India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_chess#India "History of chess") as *[chaturaṅga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chaturanga "Chaturanga")*;[[435]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolpert20032-467) There has been a rise in the number of Indian [grandmasters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grandmaster_(chess) "Grandmaster (chess)").[[436]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTERediff_2008_b-468) [Viswanathan Anand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viswanathan_Anand "Viswanathan Anand") became the undisputed [Chess World Champion in 2007](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Chess_Championship_2007 "World Chess Championship 2007") and held the status until 2013.[[437]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-469) [Parcheesi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parcheesi "Parcheesi") is derived from *[Pachisi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pachisi "Pachisi")* another traditional Indian pastime, which in early modern times was played on a giant marble court by [Mughal emperor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mughal_Empire "Mughal Empire") [Akbar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akbar "Akbar").[[438]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBinmore200798-470)

[Cricket](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cricket_in_India "Cricket in India") is the most popular sport in India.[[439]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-471) [India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India_national_cricket_team "India national cricket team") is one of the more successful cricket teams, having won two [Cricket World Cups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup "Cricket World Cup"), three [T20 World Cups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Men's_T20_World_Cup "Men's T20 World Cup"), and three [Champions Trophies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ICC_Champions_Trophy "ICC Champions Trophy"). [India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India_men's_national_field_hockey_team "India men's national field hockey team") has won a record eight [field hockey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Field_hockey "Field hockey") gold medals in the [summer Olympics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Field_hockey_at_the_Summer_Olympics "Field hockey at the Summer Olympics").[[440]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-472)

- [![The Indian hockey team, captained by Dhyan Chand (standing second from l.), after winning the finals at the 1936 Summer Olympics – their third of six consecutive Olympic golds](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Indian-Hockey-Team-Berlin-1936.jpg/330px-Indian-Hockey-Team-Berlin-1936.jpg)](File:Indian-Hockey-Team-Berlin-1936.jpg "The Indian hockey team, captained by Dhyan Chand (standing second from l.), after winning the finals at the 1936 Summer Olympics – their third of six consecutive Olympic golds")

  The Indian hockey team, captained by [Dhyan Chand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dhyan_Chand "Dhyan Chand") (standing second from l.), after winning the finals at the [1936 Summer Olympics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1936_Summer_Olympics "1936 Summer Olympics") – their third of six consecutive Olympic golds
- [![Gukesh Dommaraju, the reigning world chess champion](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/President_of_Bharat_Smt._Droupadi_Murmu_confers_Major_Dhyan_Chand_Khel_Ratna_Award_on_Shri_Gukesh_Dommaraju.jpg/120px-President_of_Bharat_Smt._Droupadi_Murmu_confers_Major_Dhyan_Chand_Khel_Ratna_Award_on_Shri_Gukesh_Dommaraju.jpg)](File:President_of_Bharat_Smt._Droupadi_Murmu_confers_Major_Dhyan_Chand_Khel_Ratna_Award_on_Shri_Gukesh_Dommaraju.jpg "Gukesh Dommaraju, the reigning world chess champion")

  [Gukesh Dommaraju](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gukesh_Dommaraju "Gukesh Dommaraju"), the reigning world chess champion[[441]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-guardian-gukesh-473)
- [![Indian cricket player Sachin Tendulkar, the highest run-getter in test cricket, playing a defensive stroke against Australia in Bangalore, 2010](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Sachin_defends_the_ball.jpg/500px-Sachin_defends_the_ball.jpg)](File:Sachin_defends_the_ball.jpg "Indian cricket player Sachin Tendulkar, the highest run-getter in test cricket, playing a defensive stroke against Australia in Bangalore, 2010")

  Indian [cricket](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cricket "Cricket") player [Sachin Tendulkar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sachin_Tendulkar "Sachin Tendulkar"), the highest [run](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Run_(cricket) "Run (cricket)")-getter in [test cricket](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Test_cricket "Test cricket"), playing a defensive stroke against Australia in [Bangalore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bangalore "Bangalore"), 2010

3. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-8) "[...] *Jana Gana Mana* is the National Anthem of India, subject to such alterations in the words as the Government may authorise as occasion arises; and the song *Vande Mataram*, which has played a historic part in the struggle for Indian freedom, shall be honoured equally with *Jana Gana Mana* and shall have equal status with it."[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConstituent_Assembly_of_India1950-7)
4. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-11) According to [Part XVII of the Constitution of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Part_XVII_of_the_Constitution_of_India "Part XVII of the Constitution of India"), [Hindi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_Hindi "Standard Hindi") in the [Devanagari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Devanagari "Devanagari") script is the [official language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Official_language "Official language") of the Union, along with [English](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_English "Indian English") as an additional official language.[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTENational_Informatics_Centre2005-1)[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinistry_of_Home_Affairs_1960-9)[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-india.gov.in2-10) [States and union territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/States_and_union_territories_of_India "States and union territories of India") can have a different official language of their own other than Hindi or English.
5. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-14) Not all the state-level official languages are in the eighth schedule and not all the scheduled languages are state-level official languages. For example, the [Sindhi language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sindhi_language "Sindhi language") is an 8th scheduled but not a state-level official language.
6. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-15) [Kashmiri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kashmiri_language "Kashmiri language") and [Dogri language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dogri_language "Dogri language") are the official languages of [Jammu and Kashmir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(union_territory) "Jammu and Kashmir (union territory)") which is currently a [union territory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_territory "Union territory") and no longer the [former state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(state) "Jammu and Kashmir (state)").
7. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-17)

In addition, there are 32 living non-indigenous languages.[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-16)
   - Different sources give widely differing figures, primarily based on how the terms "language" and "dialect" are defined and grouped.
8. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-20) "The country's exact size is subject to debate because some borders are disputed. The Indian government lists the total area as 3,287,260 km2 (1,269,220 sq mi) and the total land area as 3,060,500 km2 (1,181,700 sq mi); the United Nations lists the total area as 3,287,263 km2 (1,269,219 sq mi) and total land area as 2,973,190 km2 (1,147,960 sq mi)."[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTELibrary_of_Congress2004-19)

[↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-35) The [Government of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_India "Government of India") also regards [Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Afghanistan "Afghanistan") as a bordering country, as it considers all of [Kashmir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kashmir "Kashmir") to be part of India.[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-34) However, this is [disputed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kashmir_conflict "Kashmir conflict"), and the region bordering Afghanistan is administered by Pakistan.
12. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-51) "A Chinese pilgrim also recorded evidence of the caste system as he could observe it. According to this evidence the treatment meted out to untouchables such as the Chandalas was very similar to that which they experienced in later periods. This would contradict assertions that this rigid form of the caste system emerged in India only as a reaction to the Islamic conquest."[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKulkeRothermund2016122–123-50)
13. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-94) "All these achievements are dwarfed, though, by the Sanskrit linguistic tradition culminating in the famous grammar by Pāṇini, known as the Aṣṭhādhyāyī. The elegance and comprehensiveness of its architecture have yet to be surpassed by any grammar of any language, and its ingenious methods of stratifying out use and mention, language and metalanguage, and theorem and metatheorem predate key discoveries in western philosophy by millennia."[[81]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Evans-2009-93)
14. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-96) the historic religion of the [Vedas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vedas "Vedas"), and the precursor to [Hinduism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hinduism "Hinduism")
15. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-100) The Mauryan economy was helped by the rise of Buddhism and Jainism, creeds that promoted nonviolence, proscribed ostentation, or superfluous sacrifices and rituals, and reduced the costs of economic transactions; by coinage that increased economic accommodation in the region; and by the use of writing, which might have boosted more intricate business dealings.[[85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoy201228-99)
16. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-102) To promote movement and trade, the Mauryans built roads, most prominently a chiefly winter-time road—the Uttarapath—which connected eastern Afghanistan to their capital [Pataliputra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Patliputra "Patliputra"), during the time of year when the water levels in the intersecting rivers were low, and they could be easily [forded](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ford_(crossing) "Ford (crossing)").[[86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEIori2023184,_219-101)
17. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-117) When [Harsha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harsha "Harsha") of [Kannauj](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kannauj "Kannauj"), who ruled much of the Indo-Gangetic Plain from 606 to 647 CE, attempted to expand southwards, he was defeated by the [Chalukya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chalukya_dynasty "Chalukya dynasty") ruler of the Deccan. When his successor attempted to expand eastwards, he was defeated by the [Pala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pala_Empire "Pala Empire") king of [Bengal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bengal "Bengal"). When the Chalukyas attempted to expand southwards, they were defeated by the [Pallavas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pallava_dynasty "Pallava dynasty") from farther south, who in turn were opposed by the [Pandyas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pandya_dynasty "Pandya dynasty") and the [Cholas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chola_dynasty "Chola dynasty") from still farther south.[[100]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStein2010115–116-116)
18. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-123) Central Asian warriors became supreme during South Asia's medieval transition by deploying swift-horse cavalry skilled in firing arrows at full gallop, volley after volley.[[105]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-FOOTNOTELudden201487-122)
19. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-189) The northernmost point under Indian control is the disputed [Siachen Glacier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siachen_Glacier "Siachen Glacier") in [Jammu and Kashmir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jammu_and_Kashmir_(union_territory) "Jammu and Kashmir (union territory)"); however, the [Government of India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government_of_India "Government of India") regards the entire region of the former princely state of Jammu and Kashmir, including [Gilgit-Baltistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilgit-Baltistan "Gilgit-Baltistan") administered by Pakistan, to be its territory. It therefore assigns the latitude 37° 6′ to its northernmost point.
20. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-213) A biodiversity hotspot is a [biogeographical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biogeography "Biogeography") region which has more than 1,500 [vascular plant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vascular_plant "Vascular plant") species, but less than 30% of its primary habitat.[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-SivaperumanVenkataraman2018-212)

[↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-243) During the last years of [British rule](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Raj "British Raj"), elections were held in 1946 in all [provinces of British India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidencies_and_provinces_of_British_India "Presidencies and provinces of British India").[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-240) The Congress won electoral victories in eight of 11 provinces.[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-241) A Congress-led government was formed in September; Jawaharlal Nehru served as interim prime minister.[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Gopal1976-242)
22. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-247) Congress had the support of [left-leaning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Left-wing_politics "Left-wing politics") parties and MPs who opposed the BJP.

24. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-370) Caste is a form of [social stratification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_stratification "Social stratification") characterised by [endogamy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endogamy "Endogamy"), hereditary transmission of an occupation, ritual status in a hierarchy, and customary social interaction or exclusion defined by cultural notions of purity and pollution.[[346]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-caste-lead-369)
25. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-416) Ancient and medieval Indian mathematical works, all composed in [Sanskrit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sanskrit "Sanskrit") usually consisted of two sections: *[sutras](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sutra "Sutra")* in which a set of rules or problems were stated with economy in verse, and a prose commentary that explained the problem in more detail and provided justification for the solution.[[390]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-plofker-414)[[391]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-filliozat-p140to143-415)

27. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-433) Among young urban middle-class women, for example, a proficiency in classical dance is sometimes a sought-after social achievement.[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-vatsyayan-lord-432)
28. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-434) The classical status increases a dance's visibility and attracts more funding from agencies and ticket purchases from audiences.[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-vatsyayan-lord-432)
29. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-435) Given the geographical distribution of the chosen dances and their stylistic range, the choices could be seen as a facet of India's ethos of national integration.[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-vatsyayan-lord-432)
30. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-437) As per the [Madras Devadasis (Prevention of Dedication) Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madras_Devadasis_(Prevention_of_Dedication)_Act "Madras Devadasis (Prevention of Dedication) Act") after agitation from the Indian middle and upper classes.[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-vatsyayan-lord-432)
31. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-449) The [Central Asian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia "Central Asia") custom of buying bread outside the home accompanied the [Mughals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mughal_Empire "Mughal Empire") to India.[[418]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-bloomsbury-indian-khameri-roti-448)
32. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-466) Genetic studies have shown that mangos were first domesticated in the region between northeastern India, northwestern Myanmar, and Bangladesh.[[433]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Kuhn-464)[[434]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_note-Warschefsky-465)

[↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-31) [Metcalf & Metcalf 2012](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#CITEREFMetcalfMetcalf2012), p. 327: "Even though much remains to be done, especially in regard to eradicating poverty and securing effective structures of governance, India's achievements since independence in sustaining freedom and democracy have been singular among the world's new nations."
22. [↑](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-stein-arnold_32-0) [Stein, Burton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burton_Stein "Burton Stein") (2012). [Arnold, David](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Arnold_(historian) "David Arnold (historian)") (ed.). *A History of India*. The Blackwell History of the World Series (2nd ed.). Wiley-Blackwell. "One of these is the idea of India as 'the world's largest democracy', but a democracy forged less by the creation of representative institutions and expanding electorate under British rule than by the endeavours of India's founding fathers – Gandhi, Nehru, Patel and Ambedkar – and the labours of the Constituent Assembly between 1946 and 1949, embodied in the Indian constitution of 1950. This democratic order, reinforced by the regular holding of nationwide elections and polling for the state assemblies, has, it can be argued, consistently underpinned a fundamentally democratic state structure – despite the anomaly of the Emergency and the apparent durability of the Gandhi-Nehru dynasty."

26. [1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-Dyson2018p1_37-0) [2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-Dyson2018p1_37-1) [3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-Dyson2018p1_37-2) [Dyson 2018](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#CITEREFDyson2018), p. [1](https://books.google.com/books?id=3TRtDwAAQBAJ&pg=PA1): "Modern human beings—*Homo sapiens*—originated in Africa. Then, intermittently, sometime between 60,000 and 80,000 years ago, tiny groups of them began to enter the north-west of the Indian subcontinent. It seems likely that initially they came by way of the coast. [...] it is virtually certain that there were *Homo sapiens* in the subcontinent 55,000 years ago, even though the earliest fossils that have been found of them date to only about 30,000 years before the present."
27. [1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-Fisher2018p23_38-0) [2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#cite_ref-Fisher2018p23_38-1) [Fisher 2018](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India#CITEREFFisher2018), p. [23](https://books.google.com/books?id=kZVuDwAAQBAJ&pg=PA23): "Scholars estimate that the first successful expansion of the *Homo sapiens* range beyond Africa and across the Arabian Peninsula occurred from as early as 80,000 years ago to as late as 40,000 years ago, although there may have been prior unsuccessful emigrations. Some of their descendants extended the human range ever further in each generation, spreading into each habitable land they encountered. One human channel was along the warm and productive coastal lands of the Persian Gulf and northern Indian Ocean. Eventually, various bands entered India between 75,000 years ago and 35,000 years ago."
